# Toras Menachem Vol 05

Toras Menachem

## – 5 – 5712 – Part Two

## Title Page

### Title Page

Farbrengens
(Purim - The Second Day of Shavuos)

## Purim, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

"The Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor." Our Sages of blessed memory state in the Gemara: "Light" refers to Torah; "gladness" refers to Yom Tov; "joy" refers to circumcision; and "honor" refers to tefillin. On the face of it, the reason these four things are mentioned is because Haman’s decree was specifically intended to abolish these four things from Israel, as is stated in Targum Sheni and the Midrash. Haman decreed specifically against these mitzvos because they are signs between Hashem and the Jewish people. Therefore, when the decree was annulled, the Jews had "light"—Torah, "gladness"—Yom Tov, "joy"—circumcision, and "honor"—tefillin, as they were able to fulfill these mitzvos in their entirety and with strength [especially since this came about after they had stood with mesiras nefesh for the fulfillment of these mitzvos for nearly a year]. Nevertheless, we see that in practice, the days of Purim specifically commemorate the first two: light and gladness—Torah and Yom Tov. The matter of Torah is expressed in the very writing of the Megillah, regarding which it is said, "Write this as a memorial in a book"—meaning the addition of a new book to the Torah Shebichtav—as well as the obligation to read it on Purim, which is an act of reading from the Torah. Similarly, the Yom Tov of Purim is the essence of the days of Purim in a simple sense, as they were established as days of feasting and gladness.

2) To understand why a memory remains specifically of these two matters—Torah and Yom Tov, light and gladness—we must explain the essence of the days of Purim. Our Sages of blessed memory state regarding the verse, "The Jews confirmed and accepted," that they confirmed what they had already accepted at the Giving of the Torah. At the time of the Giving of the Torah, there was the matter of "coercing the mountain like a barrel," and therefore, "from here, a great protest against the Torah" (for they had no choice; they were coerced). But afterwards, they returned and accepted it in the days of Achashverosh through their mesiras nefesh throughout the year; meaning, at that time, the acceptance of the Torah was of their own free will. From this, we understand why "light" is defined as Torah: because on Purim, the confirmation of the acceptance of the Torah took place, and with even greater intensity and strength. The same applies to the second matter, "gladness"—Yom Tov, which is a primary element of the days of Purim. Our Sages of blessed memory state that all the festivals will be nullified in the time to come, but the days of Purim will never be nullified. Regarding this, it is said, "And these days of Purim shall not pass from among the Jews, nor shall their memory perish from their descendants." Thus, the Yom Tov of Purim is more potent than the other Yomim Tovim. Furthermore, even in the present time, the obligation of gladness on a Yom Tov ("And you shall rejoice in your festival") has a limitation, as per the halachic ruling that one should not overindulge in wine, etc.—that the Beis Din is obligated to station guards during the festivals to patrol, etc., so that people do not gather there, etc., to eat and drink and come to [transgression], etc., and not overindulge in wine, etc., in order to ensure that the gladness remains within limits. This is not the case with the gladness of Purim; not only is it permitted to overindulge in wine, but there is an explicit obligation: "A person is obligated to become intoxicated on Purim until he does not know, etc."—and the meaning of *lebasumei* is to become intoxicated—and furthermore, the measure of the obligation is "until he does not know, etc."

3) To understand all this, we must first preface what has been explained in many places regarding the superiority of the Yom Tov and gladness of Purim over the other festivals. The statement that all festivals will be nullified in the time to come means that since the revelations in all the festivals are from a level within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, and in the time to come there will be a revelation of a level that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the revelations of the festivals will be nullified before the greatness of that future revelation, like a candle in the presence of a torch. It is obvious that one cannot say that the festivals will be nullified literally, Heaven forbid, for it is a clear and explicit matter in the Torah that "this Torah shall not be exchanged, and nothing of it shall be nullified." Rather, the meaning is that the revelation of the festivals will be nullified in the face of the revelation that will be then, like a candle in the presence of a torch. [One might also explain this according to the simple meaning. The Rambam writes that in the time to come (in the days of Moshiach), all human needs will be provided in abundance, and there will be no worries about satisfying one's needs, and Israel will be able to occupy themselves with Torah. According to the simple meaning, this is the reason for the gladness of Yom Tov, which does not exist on weekdays; for on weekdays, a person is occupied with the work of the mundane, whereas on Yom Tov, there is an obligation of cessation—"you shall do no work therein (except for the work of preparing food)." Therefore, there is a special gladness on Yom Tov. However, in the time to come, when even on weekdays they will not be occupied with mundane work, as it is written, "And strangers shall stand and feed your flocks, etc.," the matter of gladness and rest of Yom Tov will not be distinct from the weekdays. This is the meaning of "all festivals will be nullified"—that the gladness of Yom Tov will not have anything special about it compared to the other days.] With this, we can understand why the days of Purim are not nullified in the time to come: because the revelation of the days of Purim is not like the revelation of the other festivals—a revelation within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—but rather a revelation that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, "until he does not know." Therefore, that revelation will not be nullified by the revelation that will be then, like a candle in the presence of a torch.

4) To understand all this in greater detail, it is known that the entirety of the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is divided into four parts: Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah. This is what is written: "Everyone who is called by My name, and for My glory I have created him, I have formed him, even I have made him." "Created him, formed him, even I have made him" refers to the three worlds of BYA: the world of Asiyah, whether physical or spiritual (the world of the spheres), and above it the world of Yetzirah, which is the world of the angels, and above it the world of Beriah, which is the world of the *neshamos*. The difference between them is also understood from their names: the matter of *Beriah* (creation) indicates the bringing into being of *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing), as the Ramban writes. In contrast, the matter of *Yetzirah* (formation) is only that which gives form to an existing thing—meaning the material exists beforehand, and the former gives it form. The matter of *Asiyah* (making) is the completion and perfection of the thing. This is also what is meant by the verse "even I have made him," which is a term of innovation (not only "created him, formed him," but "even I have made him"), because in the matter of *Asiyah*, there is a special innovation: not only is the material present (created him) and not only the form (formed him), but a physical thing is actually brought into being. It is known that through the *hishtalshelus* of cause and effect, it is impossible for physical existence to be brought into being from spirituality; therefore, the matter of the world of *Asiyah* is a completely new innovation. From the perspective of the spiritual world of *Asiyah*, the world of *Asiyah* is also included in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—worlds that evolved one from another—but from the perspective of the physical world of *Asiyah*, there is a completely new innovation here: "even I have made him," "even" implies a break. As is known, the bringing into being of physicality is not through the *hishtalshelus* of cause and effect, but the bringing into being is through the power of the *Ein Sof*, which is not an effect of any cause or reason that preceded it, Heaven forbid; therefore, He alone has the power and ability to create *yesh me'ayin* and absolute nothingness. [According to this, it turns out that the fact that the matter of *Asiyah* is included in this verse, "made him," refers to spiritual *Asiyah*, and what is written "even" implies a break, referring to physical *Asiyah*].

Regarding the matter of *yesh me'ayin*, the question is known: how can it be said that creation is *yesh me'ayin* when the true reality is above? If so, how can it be called *yesh me'ayin*? It is explained that this is because the bringing into being is only from a radiance that is drawn from Him, may He be blessed, for the essence of *Elokus* is not that the worlds are brought into being from Him, and this radiance is in the category of *Ayin* (nothing) relative to Hashem Himself. Furthermore, even relative to the created *yesh*, this level is called *Ayin*, because it is impossible for there to be a bringing into being of a *yesh* reality that feels itself to be a *yesh* and a separate thing if it feels its source. Therefore, this radiance is called *Ayin* relative to it—meaning it is not known or revealed to it. For if this radiance, which is the source of vitality, were in revelation within the created being, the created being would be nullified from its existence entirely and would be consumed and included in the light that brings it into being. Regarding this, our Sages of blessed memory said, "The Holy One, blessed be He, stretched out His little finger between them and burned them," for in the revelation of the level of His "little finger"—the source of the created beings—the created beings are nullified from their existence.

The first world that was created is the world of *Beriah*, the world of *neshamos*, which is the world of the *neshamos* of Israel. Our Sages of blessed memory said, "Israel arose in the thought, etc.," and the world of *Beriah* is called the world of thought. Just as it is below, where the beginning of the existence of letters is in thought—before the thought, even though there is a source for the letters hidden in the *nefesh*, the letters are not in the category of existence—whereas in the world of thought, there is already a felt existence of letters. From this, it is understood above as well, that the mode of the bringing into being of the *neshamos* is that they become the existence of a created being. However, just as thought is not a separate garment from a person, so too the *neshamos* above are always in a state of *ahavah* and *yirah* toward *Elokus*, as it is written, "As Hashem lives, before whom I have stood," which refers to the *neshamah* while it is above. Just as thought is not a separate thing from the person thinking, but is always connected and joined with him, and others do not know about it, so too the *neshamah* is in constant *dveikus* with *Elokus*. Below this is the world of *Yetzirah*, which is like the world of speech, for the letters of speech are a separate thing from the person, and they are in revelation to others. Similarly above, in the world of *Yetzirah*, which is the world of the angels, for the angels are brought into being from speech, as it is written, "By the word of Hashem the heavens were made, and by the breath of His mouth all their host," and therefore the angels are a separate existence, to the point that it is possible for there to be a matter of sin in them, etc. Below this is the world of *Asiyah*, "even I have made him," which refers to the world of the spheres, down to the physical and material world, which is the matter of the bringing into being of physical *yesh*. The root of this creation is from a level above "created him" and "formed him," as mentioned above, that the bringing into being of physicality is from the *Atzmus*.

Before this, it is written, "Everyone who is called by My name and for My glory." It is explained that "My name and My glory" refers to the ten *Sefiros* of the world of *Atzilus*. Seemingly, it is wondrous how it is possible that from the One of Truth, who is alone and there is none besides Him, there could be the bringing into being of a multitude of created beings, "created him, formed him, even I have made him." It is explained that in order for the multitude of details of the *Seder Hishtalshelus* to come into being from the true unity, there must be a medium. The matter of the medium in general is the ten *Sefiros* of *Atzilus*, of which it is said, "He and His life-force are one; He and His attributes are one," and therefore they are a medium between "He" and the worlds of BYA that are brought into being through the *Sefiros*. It is not meant, Heaven forbid, that the ten *Sefiros* are called a medium because the value of the ten *Sefiros* relative to the *Atzmus* is like the value of the created worlds relative to the ten *Sefiros*, for it is known that relative to the *Atzmus*, *Atzilus* and *Asiyah* are exactly equal. Rather, they are called a medium only because the ten *Sefiros* are the means through which is drawn from the true unity to the multitude of worlds of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. This is "Everyone who is called by My name and for My glory, etc.," for the emanation of the world of *Atzilus* is only so that there will be a medium for the bringing into being of the worlds of BYA, "created him, formed him, even I have made him." And all the worlds were created for the sake of man, as it is written, "I made the earth and created man upon it," so that man would fulfill the 613 *mitzvos* ("created" is *gematria* 613). From this it is understood that all the levels above—both the ten *Sefiros* of *Atzilus* and the worlds of BYA, and even the level of "Everyone who is called by My name and for My glory"—since all of this is a means for the fulfillment of the 613 *mitzvos* by man, all of this depends on the standing and state of man in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*.

5) It is known that the *Chochma* of *Atzilus* is the beginning of revelation, as it is written, "The beginning of *Chochma*," in which is the essence of the revelation of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed. As explained in Tanya in the *Hagah*, the enclothement of the *Ohr Ein Sof* in the ten *Sefiros* of *Atzilus* is through its enclothement first in the *Sefirah* of *Chochma*, because the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed, is the One of Truth who is alone and there is none besides Him, and this is the level of *Chochma*. The level of *Chochma* is *bitul*, and the light of the *Ein Sof* does not dwell except in a place that is completely nullified, and this is the level of *Chochma*. It is also known that one of the interpretations of the *Maamar* of the *Tikkunim*, "He and His life-force are one," is that "His life-force" refers to the *mochin*, and specifically the *Sefirah* of *Chochma*, which are like "His life-force"—light without vessels. That is, his feeling is that he is nothing but a revelation so that through him there will be the matter of "created him, formed him, even I have made him," and besides this, he feels nothing, only that He alone is, and there is none besides Him.

After the light of the *Ein Sof* is drawn into the *Sefirah* of *Chochma* and the *mochin* in general, in order for there to be from this the *Seder Hishtalshelus* of "created him, formed him, even I have made him"—which is the matter of thought, speech, and action as mentioned above—this is through enclothement first in the level of the *midos*. Just as it is in man below, to distinguish with infinite distinctions, that for the matter in the mind to come into thought, speech, and action, it must come through the *midos* in the heart. At first, there is the desire and will in the heart, and only afterwards is it drawn into the letters of thought—that he should contemplate how to reach the desired matter—and from the letters of thought, it is drawn afterwards into the letters of speech, such as when he commands another to bring him the desired thing, or in the matter of action, that he does the desired thing. As all this is explained in the Tanya, that at first the matter exists as it is in the power of the *Chochma* and intellect and knowledge of the person who knew the matter, and afterwards the matter is drawn into the heart so that there will be a longing and desire in his heart for the thing, and afterwards it returns and rises to the mind to contemplate it, for only then are the letters of thought born in the mind. From this, it is drawn afterwards into speech and action. From this, it is understood similarly (to distinguish with infinite distinctions) above, that in order for the Divine light to be drawn to be "created him, formed him, even I have made him," there must be a *Seder Hishtalshelus* within the ten *Sefiros* themselves: from *Chochma*, which is the beginning of intellect and the beginning of knowledge, the light must descend and be enclothed in the level of the *midos*. And from the *midos*, the light is drawn into the *Sefirah* of *Malchus*, which is thought, speech, or action. And all this is so, even though the letters of thought and speech are not brought into being from the *midos*, as we see in man below: even a small child who has *midos* cannot speak yet until he grows a little and the power of intellect is revealed in him, which proves that the bringing into being of the letters is from the intellect. In a small child, we see that the drawing of *midos* in him is with very great intensity, as we see that when a child wants something, there is no measurement or limitation in it, and he cries and screams and demands and it is impossible to calm him, and yet he cannot speak. From this it is proven that the bringing into being of the letters is not from the *midos*. Similarly, one cannot say that their bringing into being is from the revealed intellect, for we see that even when the child grows a little and has some intellect and understanding, he still cannot speak in the letters of speech, which proves that even his letters of thought are not as they should be. Only when he grows even more, and there is added to him the revelation of the source of intellect, the level of *Chochma*, or the essence of the *nefesh*, only then can he speak. From all this it is proven that the bringing into being of the letters is not from the *midos* nor from the revealed *mochin*, but from the essence of the *nefesh* and from the *mochin* as they are above revelation. But on the other hand, the content of the letters that he thinks and speaks about is a matter that he has a drawing toward, which is the matter of the *midos*. From this it is proven that for the matter of the letters, two things are needed: the bringing into being of the letters is from *Chochma*—"*Abba* founded the daughter," the *Sefirah* of *Chochma*, the essence of the *nefesh*—but in order for the letters to come into revelation, one must connect the essence of the *nefesh* with the power of thought and the power of speech, and this is done by the *midos* in the heart, which act to create division and *tzimtzum* in the revelations drawn from *Chochma*, until they can be drawn into the letters of thought and the letters of speech. An example of this is understood above: in order for there to be the matter of "created him, formed him, even I have made him," there must first be the matter of "Everyone who is called by My name and for My glory," meaning not only the matter of *Chochma Ila'ah*, which is the beginning of revelation, the beginning of *Chochma*, but also the matter of the *midos*. The reason for this is because when the letters are in the *Sefirah* of *Chochma*, they are there in a state of absolute *bitul*, as explained above that the matter of *Chochma* is *bitul*, and therefore it is impossible for details to emerge from this, let alone a multitude of details, and even details that contradict one another, for in *Chochma* there is the true unity. In order for letters to emerge in revelation and in multitude, and even matters that are opposed to one another and contradict one another, for this there must be the matter of the *midos*, whose general categories are *Chesed* and *Gevurah*, which gives room for separate matters, even to matters that contradict one another. From all this it is understood that for the bringing into being of the letters, the bringing into being of the *Seder Hishtalshelus* of "created him, formed him, even I have made him," two things are needed: the essence of the matter is from the *Sefirah* of *Chochma*, "*Abba* founded the daughter," but the revelation is through the *midos*, through which the matter is drawn below in absolute multitude.

6) This order in the revelation of *Elokus* in the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is as it was during the time the Beis Hamikdash existed, when matters of *Elokus* were in revelation. As explained above, all the drawing from above depends on the *avodah* of man below in the fulfillment of the 613 *mitzvos*. It can be said that this is why during the time of the Beis, when the conduct of Israel was as it should be, all the aforementioned drawings were as they should be. Therefore, there was a revelation of *Elokus* below, and Israel would pray and be answered, for everything they would ask for, whether for spirituality or for physicality, they were immediately answered. This is because at that time the revelation was through the level of the *midos* (as mentioned above). However, during the time of *galus*, it is written, "We have not seen our signs," for we cannot see the signs. The reason for this is because there is no revelation of the *midos* as it should be. The matter of *galus* is as it is written, "Because of our sins we were exiled from our land," for there is the matter of sin—from the word *chesron* (lack)—a lack in the *avodah* of man below, and this also acts above so that there will be a lack in the revelation of the *midos*. It is written, "For they have turned their back to Me and not their face," and therefore even from above there is no revelation of the inwardness of the *midos*—the face—but only the externality of the *midos*, the level of the back. Just like the simple difference between the face and the back: in the face is the essence of the revelation of vitality, and there are most of a person's senses—sight, hearing, smell, taste, and speech—whereas in the back, even though it is the same head, the matters are not in revelation there. And even the sense of touch, which is the least of the senses, the difference is noticeable even in it, for on the side of his face he will feel even something small, whereas behind him he will not. From all this, it is understood in the *avodah* of man: when the *avodah* below is in the category of the back—"they have turned their back to Me and not their face"—meaning that the action in matters of holiness and matters of *Elokus* is nothing but "the commandment of men learned by rote," or that it is lacking even in that, Heaven forbid, and they surrender the inwardness of the *midos* and the inwardness of the heart and the fervor in matters of intellect to external things, matters of this world—for when it comes to a physical and material matter, he feels its lack and it touches him and he is surrendered to it entirely, whereas regarding a spiritual matter and a matter of holiness, he does only what is necessary and what his father taught and accustomed him to, or even that does not help and he has a lack in this matter—this causes that even from above there will be the opposite of the matter of "face to face," and as it is written, "I will surely hide My face." Since from above the matter of the *midos* is not in revelation, the revelations from above are not drawn below into the letters of thought, speech, and action, and therefore "we have not seen our signs," for we pray and are not answered as we should be, both in physicality and in spirituality.

7) But regarding this, we say that the standing and state of the time of *galus* should not cause a falling of the spirit, and even that the falling of the spirit from this is great foolishness (as is explained in Chassidus), for during the time of *galus* we say, "For Abraham did not know us, and Israel did not recognize us; You, Hashem, are our Father." This means that even though there is no revelation of the level of the *midos* above—which is the matter of "Abraham did not know us," for Abraham is the *midah* of *Chesed*, the right line and the line of *Chesed*, which is the beginning of the *midos*, and during the time of *galus* there is no revelation of the *midos*. This is also what our Sages of blessed memory say regarding this verse in Maseches Shabbos, that Abraham could not defend Israel, etc. Similarly, "Israel did not recognize us," for Israel refers to *Ze'er Anpin*, which is the totality of the *midos*, which are not in revelation. Nevertheless, this should not cause a falling of the spirit, for "You are our Father," for there still exists the radiance of the level of "our Father," the radiance of *Chochma Ila'ah* (even though the medium of the level of Abraham and Israel is lacking). For the function of the medium of the *midos* is only to bring the letters into revelation, but the bringing into being of the letters themselves is from the level of *Chochma*, "*Abba* founded the daughter." And since during the time of *galus* the medium of the totality of the matter of the *midos* is lacking, there are no letters in revelation, but nevertheless, there still exists the source and root of the letters, which is in *Chochma Ila'ah*, only that it is not in revelation.

This is also why in *galus* it is said only "we have not seen our signs," that we cannot see the signs, but not that there are no signs, Heaven forbid. As is the precision of the language of our Sages of blessed memory that "the master of the miracle does not recognize his miracle," which implies that there are miracles, only that there is a lack in the recognition of the miracles. This is because the miracles are not revealed miracles, but they are miracles that one might think are enclothed in the ways of nature. For it is known that in nature itself there are two types of conduct. One is nature itself, which is that the world follows its custom: "seedtime and harvest, and cold and heat, and summer and winter, and day and night shall not cease," which is also from the will of the Creator (*Elokim* is *gematria* *HaTeva* (nature)), but due to the habit of this, that one is accustomed to seeing this thing every day and every moment and every time, it is possible to forget for a moment that this is a matter of *Elokus*, and to think that the world follows its custom, and there is no Master of the house for this palace, Heaven forbid. And the second is that in nature there are miracles enclothed in it, meaning that the miracles are not seen to the eyes of flesh but only to the eyes of the intellect. Like the miracle of Purim, that the servant angered his master and the king his wife, for to the eyes of the intellect the miracle is seen, for from the fact that that king annulled it, one sees with the eyes of the intellect that it is above nature, but to the eyes of flesh it is not seen. And this is not like the miracle of the splitting of the Red Sea, for example, which was seen to the eyes of flesh without any contemplation. These two modes of the conduct of nature exist every single day, for in addition to the conduct of nature by habit, there exists every day and every hour the matter of miracles enclothed in nature, regarding which they said that "the master of the miracle does not recognize his miracle," "we have not seen our signs." The reason for this is as mentioned above, because there is a lack in the matter of the *midos* (Abraham and Israel), which are the mediums to draw *Elokus* in revelation into the letters that are in revelation.

8) According to this, we can understand the extra superiority during the time of *galus* specifically, for "You are our Father." For at every time and every hour, and for each according to his standing and state, even when he does not have the matter of *ahavah* and *yirah*—which are the *midos* in the *avodah* of man below through which the *midos* above are drawn—nevertheless, there exists the matter of "For You are our Father." For regarding the matter of love and fear, there must be several types of contemplation: contemplation that brings love and contemplation that brings fear, and similarly contemplation to reveal the other *midos*. This matter requires several hours, as explained in Tanya that there must be toil of the *nefesh* and toil of the flesh, and there is contemplation that lasts an hour or two, and the measure of this hour is not the same for every *nefesh*. However, the length of time and the length of the *avodah* is only when the *avodah* is in the regular order of the revelation of the letters, through which the revelation of "face to face" is drawn from above, as it is written, "As water reflects the face to the face, so is the heart of man to man." This is not the case during the time of *galus*, when there is no matter of love and fear, etc.—"Abraham did not know us, and Israel did not recognize us"—nevertheless, there exists the matter of simple faith that exists in every single one of Israel, even in the simplest of the simple. As is proven from this, that when there is a trial, even the simplest of the simple sacrifices his life, because he has no doubts that would affect his connection with *Elokus*. Therefore, there is no difference what his standing and state is in *ahavah* and *yirah* and in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and he sacrifices his life immediately, and there is nothing that prevents and hides and conceals. Therefore, specifically during the time of *galus* there is the possibility to be transformed from one extreme to the other, by contemplating with simple faith that he is one with Hashem, and knowing that it is possible that this thing he is going to do, if it is not according to Torah or does not fit according to the instructions of the Torah, this separates him from His unity, may He be blessed, then he can change himself from one extreme to the other, so that it will be "For You are our Father." Furthermore, from this itself it is possible that he will come to love and fear, but this *ahavah* and *yirah* is not from below to above, but it is drawn from above, "For You are our Father," for by drawing the faith into the three garments of the *nefesh*—thought, speech, and action—this brings afterwards to love and fear in revelation, until the letters are drawn in revelation, until they pray and are answered, exactly as it was during the time of the

## Purim 5712

**A. The Rebbe Shlita washed his hands for the meal, instructed everyone to say "L'chaim," and afterwards directed that a *nigun* be played, and then delivered a *maamar* beginning with the words, "For the Jews there was light," etc.**

***

**B.** It was discussed earlier (in the *maamar*) regarding the greatness of Mordechai, "that Mordechai in his generation was equivalent to Moshe in his generation" —that he influenced all the people of his generation to stand in a state of *mesiras nefesh* throughout the entire year. For "if they had wanted to convert, Haman would have done nothing to them, as he only decreed against the Jews; rather, they surrendered themselves to death throughout the entire year, and no extraneous thought, Heaven forbid, entered their minds".

This was accomplished by Mordechai, who is called an "*Ish Yehudi*" —even though "he came from Binyamin," as the Gemara asks : "He calls him a *Yehudi*, implying he comes from Yehudah, and he calls him a *Yemini*, implying he comes from Binyamin." Among the answers given is: "In truth, he came from Binyamin; why then is he called a *Yehudi*?"—"Because he denied idol worship, for anyone who denies idol worship (which is equivalent to "admitting to the entire Torah") is called a *Yehudi*." And "*Ish* (Yehudi)"—which means "*Sar* (Yehudi)" —refers to the fact that he drew down and activated this matter ("Yehudi," one who denies idol worship and admits to the entire Torah) in all the people of his generation.

It is worth noting what is explained in *Tanya* that in order for the point of Jewishness to be awakened even in the lowest of the low, one must be brought to a test regarding faith, in such a way that he feels tangibly that this matter would separate him, Heaven forbid, from the *yichud* in the G-dliness of the Almighty. This is what Mordechai accomplished for all the people of his generation, from the greatest of the great to the lowest of the low—that they all stood in a state of *mesiras nefesh*, and even to actual *mesiras nefesh*.

**C.** We should add more detail regarding the activity of Mordechai ("*Ish Yehudi*") upon all the people of his generation—and by way of introduction:

Regarding the "*Ish Yehudi*," it is stated that he was "*in Shushan the capital*," which, being the capital city of Achashverosh who "ruled from one end of the world to the other", was the capital of the entire world. And therein occurred the miracle of Purim in such a way that "the Jews who were in Shushan gathered on the thirteenth of the month and on the fourteenth, and rested on the *fifteenth* of it, and made it a day of feasting and gladness", unlike "the rest of the Jews who were in the king's provinces, who gathered, etc., on the thirteenth day of the month of Adar and rested on the fourteenth of it, and made it a day of feasting and gladness".

Now, although the *Megillah* only specifies the difference between Shushan (on the 15th) and other cities (on the 14th), it is explained in the *Mishnah* that also "cities surrounded by a wall from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun [whether in Eretz Yisrael or outside Eretz Yisrael, though in Eretz Yisrael this is more common] read on the *15th*" (like Shushan), "for the verse says : 'Therefore the Jews of the unwalled towns who live in the unwalled cities, etc.'; since the unwalled ones read on the fourteenth, the walled ones read on the fifteenth". And "they derive (via *gezeirah shavah*) *perazi-perazi*: it is written here 'Therefore the Jews of the unwalled towns,' and it is written there 'besides the unwalled towns'; just as there it means from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, so too here it means from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun".

Regarding the explanation of the reason "why they hung the matter on the days of Yehoshua" [even though Shushan the capital was not surrounded by a wall from the days of Yehoshua, but only from the days of Achashverosh]—it is stated in the *Yerushalmi* (and brought by the *Rambam*) that "they showed honor to Eretz Yisrael, which was desolate in those days [for 'in the kingdom of Achashverosh, at the beginning of his reign, they wrote an accusation' (not to build the Beis Hamikdash), and 'then the work of building the house of G-d ceased' for a period of time, and since the redemption (from the Babylonian exile) was only afterwards, it turns out that at that time Eretz Yisrael was desolate], and (therefore) they hung it on the days of Yehoshua bin Nun," "so that they would read like the people of Shushan, and they would be considered as if they were cities surrounded by a wall, even though they are now desolate, since they were surrounded in the days of Yehoshua they read on the 15th, and there would be a remembrance for Eretz Yisrael in this miracle."

And in addition to the cities surrounded by a wall themselves—"a city and all that is adjacent to it and all that is visible with it," "adjacent even if not visible, visible even if not adjacent," "is judged as a city", that they read on the *15th*.

**D.** And the explanation of the matter according to *Chassidus* :

"Surrounded by a wall" refers to Torah, as our Sages said : "This wall is Torah," which "protects and saves". And in such a standing and state, not only is there no need to fear the enemy and the foe, but furthermore, one can fight against their enemies "on the thirteenth of it and on the fourteenth of it," and consequently, they celebrate the days of Purim on the fifteenth, on which "the moon stands in its fullness".

This is what is said of Mordechai: "An *Ish Yehudi* was in Shushan the capital"—for, being "*like Moshe* in his generation," through whom the *Torah* was given, it is understood and simple that his place was in Shushan the capital, a city *surrounded by a wall*, which signifies a standing and state where the "wall is Torah" is in its perfection.

And the activity of Mordechai—"An *Ish Yehudi* was in Shushan the capital"—was (first and foremost) regarding "the Jews who were in Shushan":

And by way of introduction, the precision in the word "*Yehudiyim*" (Jews) with two *yuds* (as it is written in this verse and in several places in the *Megillah*)—as explained by the Rebbe Rayatz in the *sicha* in the name of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, that "*Yehudiyim*" with two *yuds* refers both to those whose *yud* is from the *Nefesh Elokis*, the *Yetzer Tov*, and to those whose *yud* is from the *Nefesh Habahamis*, the *Yetzer Hara*, as per the exposition of our Sages on the verse : "And the L-rd G-d formed (*vayyitzer*) the man," "with two *yuds*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, created two inclinations, one *Yetzer Tov* and one *Yetzer Hara*."

And just as regarding the decree it is written : "that Haman said... against the *Yehudiyim* (with two *yuds*) to destroy them," because Haman wanted to destroy (not only G-d-fearing Jews, Jews of the *Yetzer Tov*, "frume Yidden," but) *all the Jews*, everyone who is called by the name Jew—so too, when "they gathered and stood for their lives", it is written : "the *Yehudiyim* (with two *yuds*) who were in Shushan gathered," meaning, that Mordechai's activity was not only upon the Jews who conduct themselves according to the *Yetzer Tov*, and to the point that the *Yetzer Tov* rules over them, but also upon the Jews who conduct themselves according to the *Yetzer Hara*, and to the point that the *Yetzer Hara* rules over them !

The reason for this is because in "Shushan the capital" *they saw tangibly*, with fleshly eyes, the miracle of the redemption in the manner of "it was turned around, that the Jews themselves ruled over those who hated them", "killing those who hated them", starting with "a man's enemies are the men of his own house", which refers to the *Yetzer Hara*, the body and the *Nefesh Habahamis*, that they should be turned to good, such that even for them the perfection of "surrounded by a wall" is achieved, "the moon stands in its fullness."

**E.** And in addition to the activity regarding "the Jews who were in Shushan," which is surrounded by a wall—Mordechai also acted upon all the Jews who were in towns that are now not surrounded by a wall, since they were surrounded by a wall in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun:

"Surrounded by a wall from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun"—signifies the perfection of the Jewish people upon their entry into Eretz Yisrael: "*Eretz*" (Land)—as our Sages said : "Why is it called *Eretz*? Because it wanted (*ratzah*) to do the will of its Creator," and "*Yisrael*"—an acronym for "*Yesh shishim ribo osiyos l'Torah*" (There are six hundred thousand letters in the Torah), corresponding to the six hundred thousand Jews, for every Jew has a letter in the Torah, which is why every Jew is in a standing and state of being "surrounded by a wall"—"this wall is Torah"—his letter in the Torah, his root and source.

However, it is possible that a Jew is in a standing and state where the "Eretz Yisrael" within him is *desolate* for the time being, and certainly he is not in a standing and state of being "surrounded by a wall."

And even in such a state, there is the activity of "Mordechai" ("An *Ish Yehudi* was in Shushan the capital")—that even those whose Eretz Yisrael is desolate for the time being can ascend to such a level that they will see with fleshly eyes (not only the decree, but also) the miracle of the redemption, like those who are in Shushan the capital, since by virtue of their *root and source* they possess the matter of "Eretz Yisrael," which wanted to do the will of its Creator, and the matter of being surrounded by this wall of Torah—like the cities that were surrounded by a wall in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, at the beginning of the entry into Eretz Yisrael (even if afterwards, over the generations, the situation changed). And furthermore, even those who are not in these cities themselves, but rather in a place adjacent to them or visible with them—are also judged as being surrounded by a wall, and it is in their power and ability to see tangibly the miracle of the redemption, and to celebrate the days of Purim like in Shushan the capital together with Mordechai and Esther.

**F.** And this matter (is not only something that was at that time, but) also constitutes (and, on the contrary, primarily) a lesson and instruction regarding the entire time of exile—which is relevant to the days of Purim, for "we are still servants of Achashverosh" :

It was mentioned above that "Mordechai in his generation was equivalent to Moshe in his generation." And since "the extension of Moshe is in every generation", and especially in the generation of the footsteps of Mashiach, in which Moshe Rabbeinu himself is revealed (as it is stated in *Tikkunei Zohar*), it is understood that the "extension of Moshe in every generation," our Rebbes, the leaders of every generation, are like Mordechai in his generation ("An *Ish Yehudi* was in Shushan the capital"), who act upon every single Jew [without regard to whether his place is in Shushan the capital or in other cities outside of Eretz Yisrael or in Eretz Yisrael even when it is in desolation and not surrounded by a wall]—to awaken and reveal within him the point of Jewishness, his essential connection with the Almighty.

And the point of the matter (as explained above in the *maamar*)—that even in the time of exile, after prophecy has ceased and even *Ruach Hakodesh* has ceased, and one is in a low standing and state such that "Avraham does not know us and Yisrael does not recognize us," nevertheless, by virtue of the matter of "for *You* are our Father", every single Jew can be turned around ("it was turned around") from one extreme to the other in a single moment and connect directly with the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, and afterwards the matters of "Avraham knows us" and "Yisrael recognizes us" are also drawn down in revelation, but the order is from above to below, that the beginning is by virtue of "for You are our Father," and afterwards come also the matters of "Avraham knows us" and "Yisrael recognizes us".

**G.** And it should be added that this matter is also relevant to the general revelation of the teachings of *Chassidus* specifically during the time of exile:

And by way of introduction, the saying of the *Tzemach Tzedek* that if our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe had been in the time of the *Amoraim*, he would have been among the greatest of the *Amoraim*; if he had been in the time of the *Tannaim*, he would have been among the greatest of the *Tannaim*; and if he had been in the time of the Prophets, he would have been among the greatest of the Prophets; but the generation was not worthy of it.

On the other hand, we see tangibly that specifically in the last generations the inner dimension of the Torah was revealed (as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* from the writings of the *Arizal*), and explained in the teachings of *Chassidus*, starting from the general teachings of *Chassidus* and specifically the teachings of *Chabad Chassidus*, in which and through which our Rebbes, the leaders, revealed to us *extremely lofty matters* that were not known in previous generations, when there was a revelation of *Ruach Hakodesh* and even a revelation of prophecy in Israel !

The reason for this —that specifically by virtue of the intensification of the darkness of exile, there is a need for an extremely great light that did not exist before.

**H.** And it can be said by way of possibility—more deeply—that this is where the matter of "for You are our Father, for Avraham does not know us and Yisrael does not recognize us" is expressed:

In the time of the Temple, when all matters were according to the order of *hishtalshelus* (chain-like progression) and in measurement and limitation—they could not receive lights and revelations that by their own nature are above being enclothed in vessels, since in the order of *hishtalshelus* "the vessel cannot contain" (in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in the additions to *Torah Or*);

Unlike in the time of exile—although there is indeed the deficiency that "Avraham does not know us and Yisrael does not recognize us," nevertheless, by virtue of this, the possibility is given that there can be a connection with "*You are our Father*," a connection of the Essence with the Essence, the essence of the soul with the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He—to whom alone one can truly say the title "*You*" —and to Him every single Jew can connect directly without regard to his standing and state, for even the lowest of the low, if he only feels that this matter touches upon his *yichud* and oneness with the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, can stand in all the tests out of *mesiras nefesh*, since even within him the *essence of the soul* exists in perfection, and thereby he awakens and reaches *the Essence* that is above, which is why, even though in the level below this it is written : "Was not Esav a brother to Yaakov?", nevertheless, "I have loved Yaakov" specifically, since in a loftier level, in His very Essence and Being, Yaakov specifically is rooted.

And therefore, specifically in the time of exile one can receive such lofty revelations that even in the time of the *Amoraim* were relevant only to individuals of distinction, in the time of the *Tannaim* were relevant only to individuals of distinction, and even in the time of the Prophets were relevant only to individuals of distinction—for, in the time of the Prophets, lights and revelations are drawn down that are enclothed in "vessels" [which is why "no two prophets prophesy in the same style", since for each of them the revelation is drawn down and enclothed in his own letters and vessels], whereas in the time of exile a connection is made with the Essence that is above lights and revelations that are enclothed in vessels.

And since specifically in the time of exile the matter of "for You are our Father" is revealed, therefore the revelation of the teachings of the general *Chassidus* occurred then, and specifically the teachings of *Chabad Chassidus*, through which the revelation is drawn down in the letters of *Chochma, Binah,* and *Da'as*, in a manner understood by the intellect, and even by human intellect, and even to the intellect of the *yud* of the second inclination.

And with this power our Rebbes, the leaders (like Mordechai in his generation and Moshe in his generation), act upon the matter of "to gather and stand for their lives" for all the Jews, "the Jews who were in Shushan," and also the Jews who were in the towns that were surrounded by a wall in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun (even though they are now desolate), and even those who are outside the cities themselves, but only in a manner of "adjacent" or "visible."

**I.** And we should add and explain the matter of "adjacent" or "visible" in relation to our Rebbes, the leaders, who are like Mordechai ("An *Ish Yehudi* was in Shushan the capital") in his generation:

"*Adjacent*"—is in the manner of holding onto the "doorknob" [as is known from the saying of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe: "He who will hold onto my doorknob, etc."], for, the holding onto the "doorknob" is not a matter of study, but rather a matter of *adjacency* only, and since the "doorknob" is on the door, he can stand even *outside*, such that on the face of it he has no connection to the matter, but nevertheless, he is "adjacent to it."

And at the very least "*visible* (even if not adjacent)"—that when one looks at the city surrounded by a wall, one also sees him, because he helped and assisted in the activities of the "*Ish Yehudi*" who was in the city surrounded by a wall, and consequently, when one looks at the city surrounded by a wall, his activity as a helper and assistant is also seen.

In any case, even those who are in a standing and state of "adjacent" or "visible" are judged as being surrounded by a wall, and they celebrate the days of Purim together with Mordechai and Esther in Shushan the capital in a standing and state of "the moon stands in its fullness."

**J.** And from the days of Purim one takes strength for the entire year, for all times and all places—that even in the time and place of exile ("we are still servants of Achashverosh") a Jew can come to a standing and state of "the moon stands in its fullness," and out of open joy, and extremely great joy, above all measurement and limitation ("until he does not know"), and furthermore, this joy continues and is drawn down until the days of Mashiach, in the days of Mashiach themselves, and also afterwards—as our Sages said : "All the festivals are destined to be nullified (in the days of Mashiach) and the days of Purim will never be nullified."

[And it is worth noting the continuation of the aforementioned saying of our Sages: "Rabbi Elazar said: Even Yom Kippur will never be nullified," meaning, that regarding Yom Kippur—which is equal to Purim also in the matter of *mesiras nefesh* —there is a dispute in the matter, but the days of Purim *according to all* will never be nullified, and there is no logic that they would be nullified, Heaven forbid.]

And the explanation for this —that in the days of Purim the movement of *mesiras nefesh* is revealed in practice, which exists even in the lowest of the low by virtue of the *essence* of the soul that is connected with the *Essence* of the Almighty, "*Atzmus* itself," and since there is *nothing above* this matter, it is in its strength and perfection forever.

And to add, that by virtue of the revelation of the inner dimension and essence of the soul, there can be, even in the time of exile, the matter of the coming of the personal Mashiach, and by combining everyone together, "they *gathered* and stood for their lives," they also bring about the general redemption, speedily in our days, through Mashiach our righteous one.

***

**K.** It was discussed above regarding the *mesiras nefesh* of the days of Purim, that even though they had the possibility to be saved from Haman's decree if they had denied (the opposite of the matter of "Jew"), Heaven forbid, for the decree was specifically against the Jews, nevertheless, the thought of doing so did not even enter their minds, even "outwardly," and they surrendered their lives for His oneness. And regarding this it is said that "these days of Purim will not pass from among the Jews, and their memory will not perish from their seed"—that at all times and in all places and in every standing and state there must be for every single Jew a connection to Purim (that he has a connection to Purim and Purim has a connection to him), which is expressed in the movement of *mesiras nefesh*.

And to add, that Purim is a weekday on which it is permitted to perform work, in which it is hinted that even when the Torah gives permission to engage in "weekday matters," and he engages in them, they demand of him *at that very time* the matter of "it was turned around," "they gathered and stood for their lives"—that every matter of Jewishness, Torah and its *mitzvos* (even a slight detail of the words of the Scribes, "and the custom of our fathers is Torah"), should be *touching to the soul* ("stood for their lives"), that it touches upon the connection of the essence of the soul with the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He.

And furthermore, even in a standing and state of concealment and hiding, as in the days of Purim, when there was a standing and state of "I will surely hide My face on that day" [as is known the precision that the language "on *that* day" in itself is a language of concealment, and "(on that day) itself" is in a manner of "hiding," and it is not enough for once, but "I will surely hide" twice]—even then he stands in *mesiras nefesh*, "stood for their lives," and thereby breaks and nullifies ("breaks through") all the concealments and hidings.

**L.** However, there are those who claim that due to several reasons they are in a standing and state of "a slave finds it comfortable in lawlessness" :

In the discourses of *Chassidus* it is explained at length the details of the differences between a Hebrew maidservant, a Hebrew slave, and a Canaanite slave, in the service of man. And it is explained there, that the matter of a "Canaanite slave" is (as the Gemara says) that "a slave *finds it comfortable in lawlessness*," meaning, that by his own nature he is in a standing and state of lawlessness and throwing off the yoke—which is the complete opposite of the movement of *mesiras nefesh*, whose matter is *bitul* (nullification) *above* reason and intellect, and the opposite of this is the matter of throwing off the yoke *below* reason and intellect.

That is to say: even when one explains to him according to intellect, and furthermore, that he himself *understands with his intellect*, that he must fulfill Torah and *mitzvos*, and he has proofs from his life and conduct that he sees with fleshly eyes the manner of conduct from above that the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* touches upon his physical good ("when one holds onto Torah and *mitzvos* it is simply better physically"), such that according to reason and intellect he understands himself that there should be "I love my master," since thereby he has "my wife and my children", children, life, and ample sustenance—nevertheless, he declares and shouts that "it is comfortable for me" and his will and desire is "*in lawlessness*," the lawlessness of throwing off the yoke!

—We find in holiness that regarding "desire" it is not relevant to ask questions ("on a desire there is no question"), and consequently, there is its counterpart also in the *kelipah*, that it is not relevant to ask questions and bring proofs according to intellect, since this is the matter of desire—"it is comfortable for me in lawlessness."

**M.** And this matter (a slave finds it comfortable in lawlessness, throwing off the yoke below reason and intellect) is the matter of *Amalek*—which is relevant to Purim, since Haman the Agagite is a descendant of Amalek —who is below all other nations of the world, as it is written : "Amalek is the first of the nations, but his end shall be destruction":

The other nations of the world—upon hearing that the Jewish people left Egypt "with a high hand" ("with the whole storm"), and the Almighty led them and performed for them miracles and wonders, etc.—"the peoples heard, they trembled; pangs have taken hold of the inhabitants of Peleshes, etc., then they were terrified, etc., terror took hold of them, etc., fear and dread fell upon them (upon the distant ones) and terror (upon the near ones), etc." (as all the details of the matters that were said in "Then Moshe sang"), and furthermore, knowing that when the Jewish people would come to conquer their land ("they said, 'Against us they are coming to destroy us and to inherit our land'") they would not be able to stand against them in war, and they would have to give all that they had, they searched for stratagems how to save their money, and even "hid caches of gold in the walls of their houses".

Unlike Amalek—even though he also knew about the miracles and wonders that were performed for the Jewish people, and especially that he was "a descendant of Nimrod the wicked" who "knew his Master, etc.", nevertheless, immediately after the Jewish people left Egypt (before they came to Mount Sinai) he came of his own accord to fight with the Jewish people—"And Amalek came and fought with Yisrael in Refidim" —not in order to save himself (for the Jewish people were not preparing to conquer his land), but only and solely because he wanted to *cool* the amazement and fear of *all the nations* before the Jewish people, as it is written : "who met you by the way (*asher karcha*)," a language of coolness (*kirirus*), "a parable of a boiling bath that no creature could descend into, a certain son of Belial came and jumped and descended into it, even though he was burned, he cooled it for others" —such conduct has no foundation in intellect, understanding, and comprehension (for according to intellect Amalek knew he would not be able to overcome them), but rather, a matter of *chutzpah*, "a kingdom without a crown".

And from this is taken the "chutzpah" that we find in every generation in several people—that even regarding a matter that has no place in intellect, they can be stubborn and declare that "it is comfortable for me in lawlessness."

And its counterpart in the service of man in the "war of the L-rd against Amalek from generation to generation" :

In the service of man there are obstacles and delays, concealments and hidings that come from *intellect*, and therefore, when one stands against them according to *intellect of holiness*, and argues ("he argues it out") and explains according to intellect that one must serve G-d, study Torah, and fulfill *mitzvos*, then he brings about that the concealment and hiding is nullified.

But, sometimes the inclination acts cleverly to conceal and hide (not from the side of intellect, but) from the side of *chutzpah below reason and intellect*, and then, it is impossible to stand against it through intellect of holiness,

[And especially if he engaged in the study of external wisdoms, through which he defiles the *Chabad* in his *Nefesh Elokis* (as explained in *Tanya*), meaning, that instead of utilizing intellect of holiness to stand against the *Sitra Achra*, he adds to his intellect of the *Sitra Achra*],

for, even though he understands with his intellect that he must fulfill Torah and *mitzvos*, and understands with his intellect that Torah and *mitzvos* are above intellect, and on the other hand, upon the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* depends the order of *hishtalshelus*, not only the world of *Beriah* and *Yetzirah* ("I created it, I formed it"), but also this physical and material world, as it is written : "If you walk in My statutes, etc., and I will give your rains in their time, etc."—nevertheless, he shouts that "*it is comfortable for me in lawlessness*": he cannot tolerate the bitterness of any matter that rises above him! And furthermore, he cannot tolerate such a matter also regarding his fellow, that another Jew studies Torah and fulfills *mitzvos* out of acceptance of the yoke, and therefore he strives to bring about coolness also in others ("he cooled it for others"), even though he himself is burned (as he knows himself that the lack in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* does not pay off for him simply regarding children, life, and ample sustenance)—to such an extent is the matter of "a slave finds it comfortable in lawlessness" emphasized in him!

**N.** However, in the days of Purim there is a granting of strength even regarding those who are in a standing and state of a Canaanite slave, "a slave finds it comfortable in lawlessness":

And by way of introduction—that regarding Canaanite slaves there is a dispute among the authorities whether they are obligated in the reading of the *Megillah* and other matters of Purim.

And among the lessons that they too are obligated in the matters of Purim—from what is written : "The Jews established and accepted upon themselves and upon their seed *and upon all who joined themselves to them*, etc., to be doing these two days, etc."—as explained by the *Rogatchover* that one cannot say that "who joined themselves to them" refers to converts, for "they are after the conversion like all of Yisrael."

And two details

## Vayakhel-Pekudei, Parshas HaChodesh, Mevarchim HaChodesh Nissan, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

Vayakhel Moshe et kol adas bnei Yisrael—Moshe assembled the entire congregation of the Children of Israel—and said to them, "These are the things that Hashem has commanded to do them: Six days shall work be done, and on the seventh day it shall be holy to you, a Shabbos Shabbaton to Hashem." There are well-known questions regarding this: First, what is the meaning of "Moshe assembled the entire congregation of the Children of Israel and said to them"? Seemingly, it would have sufficed to say, "And Moshe said to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel," for from that alone it is understood that he assembled them, as is stated in many places. Indeed, later regarding the construction of the Mishkan, it says, "And Moshe said to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel," from which it is understood automatically that he assembled them. So what is the purpose of "Moshe assembled"?

Furthermore, one must understand the phrase, "These are the things that Hashem has commanded to do them," without the verse specifying what these "things" are. Most commentators write that it refers to the construction of the Mishkan, which is detailed later in the parsha. But on the face of it, this interpretation is difficult, for regarding the command for the work of the Mishkan, it is written afterward yet again, "And Moshe said to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel..." If so, one must understand what "these things" are. It implies that it refers to what is stated: "Six days shall work be done," and the matter requires understanding.

Now, regarding what is stated here, "Six days shall work be done," our Sages say: "Shall be done" (te'aseh)—it shall be done by itself (mi'meila). And it is stated in the Mechilta regarding this verse: When Israel does the will of the Omnipresent, their work is done by others. Thus, immediately when Moshe began to speak with Israel, he spoke to them about an extremely lofty level in the avodah of Hashem: "doing the will of the Omnipresent." This requires explanation: what is the essence of this?

One must also understand what is stated afterward: "And on the seventh day it shall be holy to you, a Shabbos Shabbaton to Hashem." What is the meaning of "Shabbos Shabbaton"—the doubling of the language? It implies that there is an additional holiness here. Also, the connection between all the matters in these verses requires explanation: the matter of "these are the things that Hashem has commanded to do them," the matter of the command regarding Shabbos, and the matter of the assembly. And why was the assembly necessary for the command regarding the mitzvah of Shabbos, when the command of Shabbos had already been written before this several times? What was innovated here in this parsha?

2) To understand all this: In Rashi on the verse, it is stated (and so it is in the Midrash and the Zohar) that Moshe said all this on the day after Yom Kippur, when the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to him, "I have forgiven according to your word," after the atonement for the sin of the Golden Calf. The matter of the sin of the Golden Calf is that, initially, the world was created in its fullness, and afterwards the serpent came upon Chava and cast filth into her—which is the matter of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. When Israel stood at Mount Sinai, their filth ceased, and with the sin of the Golden Calf, this filth returned. Thus, on the day after Yom Kippur, after Moshe had prayed for 140 days regarding this, and there was forgiveness and atonement for the sin of the Golden Calf, Israel needed to remove the filth of the serpent from themselves through the rectification of the sin of the Golden Calf. With this, one can understand why Moshe needed to assemble all of Israel and say to them, "These are the things that Hashem has commanded to do them," for it refers to the general order of avodah in rectifying the sin. However, although Moshe said several things to them—as it says "these things" in the plural—nevertheless, the text records only one detail that also touches upon us in the avodah of man, and that is what is stated: "Six days shall work be done"—done by itself, as mentioned above.

3) The explanation of this matter is as follows: It is written, "When you eat the labor of your hands, you are fortunate, and it is good for you." Our Sages in the Mishnah say: "Fortunate" in this world, and "it is good for you" in the World to Come. The explanation of this is known: the matter of "the labor of your hands" is precise—that the occupation of earning a livelihood must be in such a way that the exertion is only of the hands, "the labor of your hands" and not your head. A person should not insert his mind and heart into the exertion of earning a livelihood, but only his hands. The mind and heart of a person must be immersed in the four cubits of Torah, the four cubits of tefillah, and the fulfillment of mitzvos, and the exertion in business is only with his hands, with the power of action alone.

This is the matter of "shall be done by itself"—that he is not troubled by the work at all; rather, it is as if the work is being done by itself. In truth, a person should not have to occupy himself with his own affairs at all, for "The earth and its fullness belong to Hashem." If so, everything is in the domain of the Holy One, Blessed be He. Moreover, it is written, "The whole earth is full of His glory," and it is written, "Do I not fill the heavens and the earth?"—where "I" refers to His very Essence. If so, when a person occupies himself with his own affairs, it is like someone who signals in front of the King. Rather, the Torah gave permission to occupy oneself with the affairs of livelihood, as it is written, "Six days you shall work and do all your work," for the Holy One, Blessed be He, established that the blessings from above should be drawn down through the person occupying himself with his needs, as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

However, since the occupation with one's own needs is only to fulfill the command of the Torah—and not because he thinks that his actions and work are what bring the livelihood by themselves—therefore, the occupation with them must be only in the manner of "the labor of your hands," and not that his mind and heart should be troubled by it. This means that the occupation with the affairs of livelihood is only with the power of action, and in that itself, only according to necessity, so that he may be a vessel for the blessing of Hashem. Furthermore, even the occupation with livelihood that is with the power of action must be for the sake of Heaven, that he should use it for the avodah of Hashem, as it is written, "In all your ways know Him."

Therefore, this occupation is called "exertion," even though he inserts into it only the power of action, because when a person does something only out of necessity and compulsion, it is called "exertion." Similarly in our case: since, from his own perspective, he does not desire this work—for he would only want to occupy himself with the affairs of Torah and mitzvos—and his occupation with livelihood is only out of necessity, as if he is being compelled, it is called "exertion." Even though the Torah gave permission for this, and there is even a mitzvah and command to occupy oneself with livelihood—as it is written, "Six days you shall work," which is a positive mitzvah—nevertheless, the person does this only because of necessity, and since he does not desire it, it is called "exertion."

Thus, there are two extremes here: on one hand, it is called "shall be done by itself," and on the other hand, it is called "exertion." On one hand, the occupation is in the manner of "the labor of your hands" and not the head and heart—he does not insert his mind and heart into it, but occupies himself with it only with the power of action according to necessity; but his will, mind, and heart are not in it, and therefore it is as if the work is being done by itself. On the other hand, even though he inserts into it only the power of action alone, and only in the necessary measure, and it is in the manner of "by itself," nevertheless, since he does not desire it, it is called "exertion."

This is "Six days shall work be done, and on the seventh day, Shabbos Shabbaton..."—that specifically when the work during the six days is in the manner of "shall be done by itself," then specifically "on the seventh day, Shabbos Shabbaton." The matter is that when the preparation on Erev Shabbos is not as it should be—meaning that his occupation with livelihood is not in the manner of "the labor of your hands" alone, but he inserts his mind and heart into it, and he is troubled by the business—then even when he detaches himself for a moment from the business and wants to occupy himself with Torah and tefillah, even then the thoughts confuse him. And not only that, because of his giving and dedication to the business throughout the day, these thoughts confuse him during Torah and tefillah, but furthermore, strange thoughts fall upon him to which he does not belong at all. Because he opened a door to these thoughts, when one opens a door, things are pushed in there. Therefore, when the day of Shabbos comes, not only does he not have the aspect of Shabbos Shabbaton—the aspect of "then you shall delight in Hashem"—but he does not even have a simple Shabbos (Shabbos once), and when he wants on Shabbos to "gaze at the glory of the King," he cannot.

The explanation is that regarding Shabbos, our Sages said: "A person should always view himself on Shabbos as if all his work is done." This can only be when his occupation with livelihood is in the manner of "the labor of your hands," where he does not insert his mind and heart into the business of livelihood. But when he is troubled by the business, it is impossible that on the day of Shabbos it should be for him as if all his work is done, and because of the business matters that he has not yet finished before Shabbos, he has confusion even on the day of Shabbos. Not so when his occupation with livelihood is in the manner of "the labor of your hands," where he is not troubled by it—"Six days shall work be done" by itself—then "on the day of Shabbos, Shabbos Shabbaton," for then there is an addition of holiness, because even during the weekdays he is on the level of Shabbos, because he is not troubled by the "work of the weekday," and when the day of Shabbos comes, it is for him Shabbos Shabbaton, where there is an addition of holiness in Shabbos itself.

4) This is "Moshe assembled the entire congregation of the Children of Israel... Six days shall work be done." We stated above that this assembly was on the day after Yom Kippur, meaning that then the rectification for the sin of the Golden Calf—the sin of idolatry—was begun. This rectification is when the occupation with livelihood is in the manner of "shall be done by itself." Regarding the sin of idolatry, the Rambam writes in explaining the error of the generation of Enosh, when it began to call upon the name of Hashem, that the generation of Enosh thought that since the influences from above come through intermediaries, as it is written, "From the bounty of the sun's crops and the bounty of the moon's yield," then even though they are only intermediaries, nevertheless, since the influence from above passes through them, they erred in thinking that they have power. Therefore, they bowed down to the sun and the moon, because they wanted to receive the influence from them. This means that they also admitted that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is the King of kings of kings, calling Him the "G-d of gods," but they considered them to be a reality. But the truth is that this is the prohibition of idolatry, that one must not consider them a reality at all, because they are nothing but an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it. More subtly, the matter of the sin of idolatry is when one thinks that there is some importance to the garments and boundaries of nature. Therefore, the rectification for this sin is when the occupation with livelihood is "by itself," without the trouble of the mind and heart. For bowing down means lowering the head, which means investing his mind in the garments of nature and the occupation of livelihood; the rectification for this is "work shall be done," done by itself, which is the opposite of lowering the head.

5) Just as it is in the occupation of livelihood, so it is also more subtly in the avodah of Hashem. It is possible to have two modes in this, as it is stated in the Mishnah: "Do not be like servants who serve the master in order to receive a reward, but be like servants who serve the master not in order to receive a reward." The avodah "in order to receive a reward" means (subtly) when he knows and understands the good and the superiority in Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos, and because of this he has pleasantness, sweetness, and delight in Torah and mitzvos, and therefore he occupies himself with them. But regarding this, they said, "Do not be like servants who serve the master in order to receive a reward," for the avodah of Hashem in its truth is not because he feels the good that he has from the avodah, but that he serves in "acceptance of the yoke" only to fulfill the Supreme Will.

Thus, this avodah of "acceptance of the yoke" is in the aspect of "shall be done by itself" and in the aspect of "exertion." Since the avodah is not because of delight, will, desire, or attraction, but only in "acceptance of the yoke" (and as if he does not desire it and does it because of compulsion), therefore this avodah is called the aspect of "exertion." But because of this, it is also in the aspect of "shall be done by itself." When the avodah is from the feeling of good, then it is possible that he will think, "My power and the might of my hand have made me this wealth," that because of the quality of his talents and the quality of his character traits, he studies Torah and gives charity. But when the avodah is not in the feeling of self, but only in "acceptance of the yoke," then he understands and feels that the avodah is not from himself, but only with Heavenly assistance, that he only opens [a path] like the eye of a needle, and then they assist him greatly from above—that the assistance is the main thing, as the saying goes: "Open for Me like the eye of a needle, and I will open for you like the entrance of a hall." This is the matter of avodah "by itself," that he feels that the matter is not done by his avodah, but that by opening like the eye of a needle, the matter is effected "by itself" from above.

This matter of "exertion by itself," which is a rectification for the sin of the Golden Calf, also contains a rectification for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, as mentioned above that the sin of the Golden Calf is the return of the filth of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. This will be understood according to what is explained elsewhere, that the essential matter of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge is the matter of "feeling," as it is written, "And the woman saw that the tree was good for food and that it was a desire to the eyes," which is the matter of feeling—that she felt the reality of herself and her desire. Therefore, the rectification for this is the matter of avodah "by itself," that the person does not feel himself to be a reality, the opposite of the feeling of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge.

With this, one can also explain what is stated elsewhere, that the souls that were in the bondage of Egypt are the souls of the Generation of Dispersion, who said, "Let us build ourselves a city and a tower..." Therefore, the rectification for this was the bondage of Egypt, where they worked with mortar and bricks. It can be said that the sin of the Generation of Dispersion, who said, "And let us make ourselves a name," was also the matter of feeling—the feeling of self—and the rectification for this is through the exile of Egypt, with mortar and bricks, in exertion. The work with mortar and bricks to build the tower was not in exertion, since they had delight in it, saying, "We will ascend to the heavens and fight Him," etc. Therefore, the rectification for this was through back-breaking labor, work that breaks the body and the soul.

And so it is regarding the rectification of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, that the rectification is through avodah in exertion, for in exchange for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, which is the matter of feeling—the opposite of "exertion by itself"—the avodah must be in "acceptance of the yoke" and from within the nullification of his reality. When the avodah is in feeling, it is not exertion, since he delights in his avodah, and it is not "by itself," because he thinks that he did all this through his avodah. Therefore, the rectification for this is "shall be done by itself," that in exchange for his avodah having been from within delight, now it is in exertion, and in exchange for his having thought "my power and the might of my hand," now it is "by itself." This is the rectification for the sin of the Golden Calf and the sin of the Tree of Knowledge: exertion by itself, both in the affairs of livelihood and in the affairs of the avodah of Hashem. In the affairs of business, this is when he does not desire it at all and occupies himself with it only out of necessity—meaning that his desire and will are in Torah and mitzvos, and his occupation is only out of necessity, as if he is being compelled. Therefore, he calculates how much time he must occupy himself with it, and only during those hours does he occupy himself with it, and even then he waits and anticipates that the time necessary for the business of livelihood will pass, so he can occupy himself with Torah and tefillah. And so it is also in the avodah of Hashem, that the avodah is from "acceptance of the yoke." In all this, there is a rectification for the sin of the Golden Calf and the sin of the Tree of Knowledge.

6) This is "Moshe assembled the entire congregation of the Children of Israel... These are the things..." On the day after Yom Kippur, when they needed to remove the filth so that the world would be as it was before the sin—for the world was created in its fullness—then "Moshe assembled... and said... These are the things," meaning the general avodah of drawing down the Shechinah below. "These are the things" refers to the 39 labors, according to the teaching of our Sages that "things" (devarim), "the things" (ha-devarim), "these are the things" (eleh ha-devarim) refers to the 39 labors for Shabbos. In general, it refers to all the "work of the weekday." In this is the command to be the drawing down of the Shechinah into the "work of the weekday."
