With this, we can understand what our Sages said in the *Midrash* : In the time to come, Hashem will make a *kinegiya* (a contest/tournament) for the *tzaddikim* with Leviathan and the *Shor HaBar* (wild ox), and Leviathan will slaughter the *Shor HaBar* with its fins. It is explained in *Likutei Torah* that the difference between Leviathan and the *Shor HaBar* is that Leviathan is among the creatures of the sea, while the *Shor HaBar* is among the creatures of the land.

Creatures of the sea are always connected to their source and swallowed up within their source; as soon as they leave the water (the sea), their source of life, they die. Furthermore, not only do they die when separated from their source of life, but even while they are within the sea, which is their source of life, they have no independent existence at all; their entire existence is their source of life. As is explained in other places regarding the reason for the opinion of Rabbi Shimon ben Gamliel that anything in the sea does not constitute a *chatzitzah* (interposition): even though they are creatures of the sea—meaning there is some existence created from the water—nevertheless, their entire existence is the water itself, and therefore they do not constitute a *chatzitzah*.

In contrast, creatures of the land can be separated from their source for a time, for "everything was from the dust" —meaning the dust is their source—yet they can be in the air for a time. And even when they are on the ground, they are not part of the existence of the dust, but are an existence unto themselves.

From this, we can also understand the *nimshal* above : the difference between the "souls of the sea" and the "souls of the land"—that is, the souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya* (the hidden world) and *Alma D'Atgalya* (the revealed world)—is that the souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya* are always included in their source, meaning they always feel their source and their entire existence is the existence of the source. In contrast, the souls of *Alma D'Atgalya*, even though they understand and grasp that their entire existence is from the source, nevertheless, they are not in a state of *bitul b'metzius* (nullification of existence).

The souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*, because they always feel their source, are in a state of actual *bitul b'metzius*, like Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, who said, "I am a sign in the world", meaning he was in a state of *bitul b'metzius* to his source. [And since he was nullified to his source in such a way that his entire existence was the existence of the source, he therefore said, "I am a sign in the world," for being the existence of the source, he was truly a great existence.] And so it is with all the souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*, who are in the category of "fish of the sea" (*nunei yama*), for they are always attached to Elokus. *Likutei Torah* there brings an example of this, such as Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai.

[In other places it is stated that this is the case with the Patriarchs. That the Patriarchs fulfilled the entire Torah before it was given does not mean they fulfilled everything in practice, but rather that they fulfilled and effected all the supernal *yichudim* that are now accomplished through physical *mitzvos*; they caused and accomplished this through their *kavanah* in the spiritual realms.] The Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, adds in a gloss to the *maamar* of the Alter Rebbe, and likewise the Baal Shem Tov. It can be said that from this, it is also understood regarding all the successors of the Baal Shem Tov, that they too are in the category of *nunei yama*, souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*. Especially the soul of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, based on the saying of the Rebbe (Rashab) that the Alter Rebbe was a soul of *Atzilus*. It is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that a soul of *Atzilus*, while below, is like it is above in *Atzilus*, and therefore, when there is some matter that is not as it should be, it does not disturb the soul of *Atzilus*.

And so it is also with souls of *Beriah*, for these souls are also called *nunei yama*. For even though, in general, *Atzilus* is *Alma D'Atkasiya* and *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* are *Alma D'Atgalya*, in more specific detail, there is a difference between the world of *Beriah* and the world of *Yetzirah*. For *Beriah* is *machshavah* (thought), *Alma D'Atkasiya*, while *Yetzirah*, which is the level of *dibbur* (speech), and *Asiyah*, the level of *ma'aseh* (action), are *Alma D'Atgalya*. From all this, it is understood for our purposes that Leviathan refers to the souls that are in the category of *nunei yama*, souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*, and they are all named after Leviathan because it is the great fish among the creatures of the sea.

However, the *Shor HaBar* are the souls of *Alma D'Atgalya*, for the souls are in the category of an ox (*shor*), creatures of the land, yet it is the *Shor HaBar* (wild ox). Regarding this, *Likutei Torah* there brings three interpretations. One interpretation: *Bar* is from the word *birur* (clarification) and *zikuch* (refinement), meaning it refers to the souls in the category of *shor* that have already been clarified and refined. Another interpretation: *Bar* is a term for grain, as in "to buy grain" (*lishbor bar*), for through the souls in the category of *shor* (*Alma D'Atgalya*), the grain comes to grow, as it is written, "And abundance of crops is by the strength of the ox." For even though the growth itself comes from the power of the *tzomei'ach* (vegetative soul)—when one sows a seed in the ground, one awakens the power of growth in the earth—nevertheless, the abundance of the growth depends on the plowing, which is through the *avodah* of the ox, "And abundance of crops is by the strength of the ox." A third interpretation of *Bar*: *Bar* is a term for "outside." And in this itself, there are two matters. One matter of "outside" is that it assists the "inside"—not only does it not contradict or hinder the inside, but on the contrary, it assists the inside. [And this is not the same as "abundance of crops by the strength of the ox," for that matter of the ox is that it is found inside and assists from within, whereas the matter of *Shor HaBar* as "outside" means it is found outside and assists the inside. This can be understood based on what is explained regarding the *birurim*: that there is a first *birur* and a second *birur*. The first *birur* is *ha'alah* (elevation), where one stands outside and ascends upward, and the second *birur* is the matter of *hiskalelus* (inclusion), where one is already inside but needs to be included. And so it is in our case: the *Shor HaBar* as "outside" is the level of the first *birur*, and the *Shor HaBar* as "grain" is the level of the second *birur*, *hiskalelus* from within.] Another matter of *Shor HaBar* as "outside" is that it opposes the inside.

It can be said that these three interpretations regarding the *Shor HaBar* correspond to the three levels of *tzaddikim*, *beinonim*, and *resha'im*. *Tzaddikim* are in the category of *birur* and *zikuch*—*Shor HaBar* as *birur*. *Beinonim* are the category of "abundance of crops by the strength of the ox," for a *beinoni* is one who has never committed a sin in his life and never will. And *resha'im* are the "outside" that contradicts the inside, for they fight against the *tzaddikim*.

### 3

Now, according to what was explained above (in the explanation of the verse "This Leviathan which You have created to sport with" and the statement of our Sages that during the last three hours He sits and sports with Leviathan) that Leviathan refers to the fact that the souls of Israel in general connect worlds and Elokus—which applies to all of Israel—we must understand how this fits with what is explained in *Likutei Torah* here, that Leviathan refers only to the souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*.

The matter is that this is what is meant by the fact that in the time to come, Leviathan will slaughter the *Shor HaBar* with its fins: that the ultimate intent of the souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya*, the category of Leviathan, is that they will elevate also the souls of *Alma D'Atgalya*, so that they too will reach this level of Leviathan—meaning not just connecting worlds and Elokus in general, but that the connection will be at the level of Leviathan, *Alma D'Atkasiya*. As is explained in *Likutei Torah* there, this is the matter of the slaughtering of the *Shor HaBar* by Leviathan.

And based on what was explained that *Shor HaBar* refers not only to *tzaddikim* and *beinonim* but also to *resha'im*, it turns out that the *tzaddikim* who are souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya* (such as the souls of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, etc., as mentioned above) elevate also the souls of the *resha'im*. For regarding the slaughtering of the *Shor HaBar*, it is known that "slaughtering" (*shechitah*) means nothing other than "drawing" (*meshech*) —that is, the drawing and elevation from one domain to another. The souls of *Alma D'Atkasiya* will influence the souls of *Alma D'Atgalya* to elevate them to their level, until they effect even the *resha'im* who fight against the *tzaddikim*, to elevate them from the domain of *Kelipah* to the domain of *Kedushah*.

This is also the meaning of the slaughtering being "with its fins" (*s'napireha*), for the fins are the wings with which it swims, which are *ahavah* and *yirah*. This means that the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *tzaddik* who is in the category of *Alma D'Atkasiya* will act also upon the *resha'im* who are rebellious and defiant toward the *tzaddikim*, to draw them and elevate them to the domain of *Kedushah*. This is the matter of the *kinegiya* that Hashem will make for the *tzaddikim* in the time to come, which will also relate to the *resha'im*—the war of the *tzaddikim* and the *resha'im*—and in the end, Leviathan will slaughter the *Shor HaBar* with its fins.

### 4

However, according to this, we must understand why this matter is for the time to come, when, on the contrary, the main war is now in this present time, and in the time to come, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth". And in this time itself, the main war is during the time of *Galus*, and especially in the footsteps of Mashiach. If so, what is the meaning of saying that the *kinegiya* will be in the time to come?

The matter is that the power to win this war comes specifically from the *Atzmus* (Essence), transcendent of the level of *oros* (lights) and *giluyim* (revelations). It is written, "Was not Esau a brother to Jacob?... yet I loved Jacob." This matter of "Esau was a brother to Jacob" is from the perspective of the *Atzmus* that is above *hishtalshelus*. For from the perspective of the *seder hishtalshelus*, it is written, "And one nation shall be stronger than the other," for when one rises, the other falls, etc. Esau’s root is from the world of *Tohu* that preceded *Tikkun*, and Jacob’s root is from *Tikkun* which clarifies *Tohu* ; this is "one nation shall be stronger than the other." Therefore, from the perspective of this level, it is not appropriate to say, "Was not Esau a brother to Jacob," for "brother" implies connection and unity, and in *hishtalshelus*, it is not appropriate to say this regarding Jacob and Esau.

Only from the perspective of that which is above *hishtalshelus*—which is above *Tohu* and *Tikkun*—is it appropriate to say, "Was not Esau a brother to Jacob." As the saying goes, "I do not know in which of them He desires." And it is written, "If you are righteous, what do you give Him? And if your transgressions are multiplied, what do you do to Him?" Specifically from the perspective of the *Atzmus* is the power given to Israel to win the war, "and I loved Jacob." For from the perspective of the *oros* and *giluyim* in the *seder hishtalshelus*, on the contrary, "the *Yetzer Hara* precedes him", and even from the perspective of that which is above the *seder hishtalshelus*, both are equal, as mentioned above, "Esau was a brother to Jacob," and therefore it is impossible to win the war.

The power for victory comes from the *Atzmus*—"If Hashem does not help him, he cannot overcome him" —which is the help and assistance from the *Atzmus*, "and I loved Jacob." This is from the perspective of the fact that the souls of Israel are rooted in the *Atzmus*. This is what is meant by "You are children to Hashem your G-d." Just as with a son below, even though the son becomes an existence unto himself, he is nevertheless one essence with the father, so too in the *nimshal* above, from the perspective of the *Atzmus*, the victory of the war can occur.

The drawing down of the power of the *Atzmus* is through the level of accepting the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, as the saying goes, "A person should always accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven first, and afterward accept upon himself the yoke of the *mitzvos*." For Torah and *mitzvos* in the *Sefiros* above are the level of *Ze'er Anpin* and *Malchus*, or *Chochmah Stima'ah* and *Arich Anpin*, all of which is the *seder hishtalshelus*. The matter of the yoke of *mitzvos* is above *hishtalshelus*, but it is still within *oros* and *giluyim*. In contrast, the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven is in the *Atzmus*. For the heavens are *makifim* (encompassing), the level of *Sovev Kol Almin*, and the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven is in the level of the *Atzmus* that is above even *Sovev Kol Almin*.

It is explained in other places that even in the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum*, there is the level of *Malchus* of *Malchus* of *Ein Sof*, and at this level, the *Tzimtzum* occurred. Just as after the *Tzimtzum* there are many levels (as mentioned above), so too before the *Tzimtzum*, in the level of the *Malchus* of *Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum*, there is the matter of *Malchus*, and there is the matter of *Keser Malchus*, which is the desire for kingship. But the souls of Israel are rooted in the *Atzmus* that is above even the level of *Keser Malchus*. This is "With whom did He consult? With the souls of the *tzaddikim*", for the souls of Israel, who are the *tzaddikim*—as it is written, "And Your people are all *tzaddikim*"—from them comes the desire for kingship above, from which it is understood that they are above even this level.

The drawing down of this level is through the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven. As is explained in the *maamarim* for *Rosh Hashanah* regarding the crowning of the King, that the crowning comes specifically through the *bitul* (nullification) of the people—not through comprehension and not through feeling, but specifically through *bitul*—for through this, one specifically awakens the desire for kingship. From this, it is understood that the revelation of this matter—that the souls are rooted in the *Atzmus* and from them comes the desire for kingship—is specifically through *kabalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke). And this leads to the victory of the war.

The revelation of the *Atzmus* will be specifically in the time to come (as explained above). This is what is meant by "And they shall no longer teach each man his neighbor... saying, 'Know Hashem,' for they shall all know Me," meaning because there will be a revelation of the *Atzmus* that is above the name *Havayah* and above *Havayah* itself. Before the world was created, there was only "He and His Name" —meaning *Havayah* Himself and the name *Havayah*. And in the name itself, there are two aspects: the revelation to Himself and the revelation as it relates to the worlds. However, in the time to come, there will be a revelation of the *Atzmus* that is above the aspect of His name and also above the aspect of "He." Therefore, this revelation will be for everyone equally. For even though there will still be differences in levels, that will be from the perspective of comprehension in the level of the name *Havayah*, but in the knowledge of the *Atzmus* that is above *Havayah*, everyone will be equal. This is "for they shall all know Me"—"Me" specifically, the knowledge of the *Atzmus*. The matter of "knowledge" here does not mean comprehension and grasp, but rather it is a matter of knowledge and connection, the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus*.

Therefore, they said in the *Midrash* that the matter of the *kinegiya* will be specifically in the time to come, because the help for this war is from the *Atzmus* (as mentioned above), and this matter will be in revelation specifically in the time to come. The reason for this is because the war is a very difficult war. And if not for the help from above, he cannot overcome him—meaning if not for the assistance from the *Atzmus*, he cannot overcome him. The reason for this is because the root of the *Shor HaBar* is extremely high, for the *Shor HaBar* is called "the beasts on a thousand mountains" (*behemos b'harrei elef*), and there are two interpretations of this : one, that it eats every day the beasts on a thousand mountains; two, that it eats the grass on a thousand mountains. From this, it is understood in the spiritual sense that the adversary is very difficult and the war is an extremely difficult war.

This is the reason why among *Chassidim* the concept of *b'derech mimila* (automatically) is not accepted. This does not mean that one just has to toil, but rather that because of the difficulty of the war, it is impossible for the victory to be *b'derech mimila*; it must be through *avodah* specifically. Therefore, the matter of the *kinegiya* is for the time to come, for now, when the *Atzmus* is in concealment, because of the difficulty of the war, it is impossible to know who will win. Therefore, since the *Beis HaMikdash* was destroyed, there is no laughter, for all matters add *oros* in *Atzilus*, but in this world, the victory has not yet arrived in practice. Specifically in the time to come will there be the aspect of the laughter in the *kinegiya*, because then the victory of the war will be in practice.

### 5

In the continuation of the matter in *Likutei Torah* there, it also brings the action of the *Shor HaBar* on Leviathan in the time to come. It can be said that the explanation for this is because through the *tzaddikim* who are from the level of *Alma D'Atkasiya*, *nunei yama*, effecting an elevation in the souls that are in the category of *Shor HaBar*, this itself effects a great elevation also in these *tzaddikim*. Similar to what is explained that the descent of the soul is not for its own sake—for the soul itself does not need refinement, and it only descended to clarify the body and the *nefesh habahamit*—but nevertheless, through its *avodah*, it has an elevation. And so it is in this matter, that through the action of the *tzaddikim* on the *resha'im*, they themselves are elevated.

Similar to the matter of "I did not eat the meat of the ox, I did not scrutinize the reason for the matter", for the scrutiny of the matter is not in the meat of the fish, but specifically in the meat of the ox, the meat of the *shor*. And this specifically brings the scrutiny of the reason for the matter, meaning the revelation of the *taamei Torah* (reasons of Torah) that will be revealed in the time to come. For then there will be the laughter in the *kinegiya*, because then there will be the revelation of the *Atzmus* and there will be the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of *Ein Sof*.

## Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Shemini, Mevarchim HaChodesh Iyar, 5712

**Unedited**

**A.** Maamar beginning "This Leviathan You created..."

**B.** The distinction between Yom Tov and Shabbos is well known — the essence of Yom Tov is *simcha*, whereas Shabbos, although it also contains the element of *simcha*, its primary essence is *taanug* (which transcends *simcha*). *Simcha* on Shabbos remains in a state of concealment, and we complete it through our *avodah* during the weekdays.

However, this applies to the Shabbosos throughout the year. It is different regarding the Shabbosos of *Yemei HaSefirah*, because the weekdays of *Sefirah* have restrictions regarding *simcha*. Consequently, it is impossible to complete the *simcha* of Shabbos during the weekdays; therefore, the revelation of *simcha* must take place *on Shabbos itself*. Moreover, the *simcha* of Shabbos must be in a manner of *addition*, so that even during the weekdays of *Sefirah* (which have restrictions regarding *simcha*), the element of *simcha* is drawn down, at the very least in concealment.

This is especially true for the Shabbos at the beginning of *Yemei HaSefirah*. Since it follows immediately after the festival of Pesach (a Yom Tov whose essence is *simcha*), its connection to the concept of *simcha* is more pronounced. It is a *simcha* that adds the virtue of Shabbos — which is "sanctified and established" by itself (regardless of the person's status or whether they are worthy of it) — to the *simcha* of Yom Tov.

A further advantage in this year’s calendar is that this Shabbos is as close as possible to the Last Day of Pesach (which fell on Thursday). The entry into Shabbos comes directly from the *simcha* of the Last Day of Pesach, without any interruption, since Friday is not a weekday, but rather "Isru Chag." In the Yerushalmi, this is called "Beriah d'Moada," meaning "a child of the festival". Like a child who, while being a distinct existence, is drawn from the father's brain and is of the father's essence (as discussed earlier in the *maamar*). Therefore, we must now continue the *simcha* of the Last Day of Pesach in order to draw it into the weekdays (*Yemei HaSefirah*) that follow.

[The Rebbe instructed to play a joyous *nigun*.]

**C.** In the *parsha* of the week, "And it was on the eighth day," the connection to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, is alluded to:

It is known that the three festivals — Pesach, Shavuos, and Sukkos — correspond to Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov: "Pesach corresponds to Avraham, as it is written, 'Knead and make cakes'; Shavuos corresponds to Yitzchak, for the *shofar* blast of the Giving of the Torah was from the ram of Yitzchak; and Sukkos corresponds to Yaakov, as it is written, 'And for his cattle he made booths'". And Shemini Atzeres, which is connected to and follows the seven days of Sukkos (which is why it is called "eighth"), corresponds to Yosef, who is connected to and follows Yaakov, as it is written, "These are the generations of Yaakov: Yosef".

Likewise, we can say regarding the *parsha* of *Shemini* — like Shemini Atzeres — that it is connected to *Yosef*. In this is hinted the connection and relationship to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, whose (first) name is *Yosef*.

**D.** The explanation of the matter:

Shemini Atzeres, besides being a continuation of the seven days of Sukkos, is also "a festival in its own right regarding the laws of *Pazar Kashav*". Moreover, its virtue is greater than the seven days of Sukkos, as explained in the Midrash: on the seven days of Sukkos, seventy bulls are offered corresponding to the seventy nations of the world, whereas on Shemini Atzeres, one bull is offered corresponding to Yisrael ("They shall be for you alone, and no stranger with you").

Similarly, Yosef (corresponding to Shemini Atzeres) — besides being a continuation and the core essence of Yaakov — his virtue is greater than that of Yaakov (and the other Patriarchs and Tribes). As explained in the *Chassidus* discourses, the reason for the difference between the *avodah* of the Patriarchs/Tribes and the *avodah* of Yosef is that the Patriarchs and Tribes were shepherds, living in a state of seclusion from worldly matters so that they would not distract them from the *avodah* of Hashem. Yosef, however, even while being "ruler over all the land of Egypt" and in the position of "he came into the house to do his work", was in a state of ultimate *dveikus* in *Elokus*. This is because Yosef was *completely above the world*, and therefore worldly matters did not distract him from the *avodah* of Hashem, as they did not occupy any space for him at all (similar to the one bull of Yisrael on Shemini Atzeres, which is above any connection to the seventy bulls of the nations of the world during the seven days of Sukkos).

For this reason, Yosef was punished for creating a vessel through natural means when he asked the chief cupbearer, "Do me a kindness and mention me to Pharaoh", whereas Yaakov, who took many actions to be saved through natural means, was not. This is because Yosef is entirely above the world, and the world holds no place for him at all.

**E.** The difference between Yosef and the Patriarchs is analogous to the difference between the Rebbe, my father-in-law, and our Rebbes who preceded him:

The previous Rebbes lived and worked in small towns, such as Liozna, Liadi, and Lubavitch — in a manner of seclusion from the world.

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, was different. From the beginning of his *nesi'us*, he was in Moscow, then in Petersburg (as it was then called, Leningrad), afterwards (upon leaving that country) in Riga, and subsequently (upon arriving in this country) in New York. There is no "tumult of a city" better (or worse...) than this. Yet in all these places, his *avodah* was similar to the *avodah* of Yosef HaTzaddik when he was ruler over all the land of Egypt.

This power the Rebbe bequeathed to *us* — that wherever we are, even in "Egypt," and "Egypt" in its full strength ("in the greatest Egypt"), not only are we not impressed at all by the strength of Egypt, but on the contrary, we engage there in spreading Torah.

**F.** This matter also relates to the *order* of *avodah*:

Someone might think that his *avodah* must follow an orderly sequence: first, think of himself and his household, and only afterwards of others. In the words of the verse, "And he shall make atonement for himself and for his house, (and afterwards) for the entire congregation of Yisrael." The answer to this is that the order of "for himself and for his house, (and afterwards) for the entire congregation of Yisrael" applies to the *avodah* of the *Kohen Gadol* on Yom Kippur in the Beis HaMikdash. However, when one is in Egypt, in the time of *galus*, in a situation of darkness, one cannot make calculations regarding the order of *avodah* — that first the work must be with oneself and one's household and only then with others. Rather, one must do everything one can immediately, without orders and without calculations.

Just as one should not make calculations regarding prioritizing *avodah* with oneself over *avodah* with others, so too one should not make calculations in *avodah* with others according to the usual order of "from the easy to the difficult," to first act on an easy matter and then on a harder one. Rather, one must do everything one can, without order and without calculations.

For example: even when speaking with a Jew whose status regarding putting on *tefillin* is unknown, one must speak with him about studying a chapter of *Tanya* before *davening*!

— In Nikolayev, there was an *maskil* who loved studying *Chassidus* and would study *Likutei Torah* on Erev Shabbos. When it became dark, he would do what one does on a weekday night...

Seemingly, there is room for wonder: How is this possible?! When I do not know his status regarding keeping Shabbos, should I speak to him about studying *Tanya*?!...

The answer to this is that we are in a time of a fire, *chas v'shalom*, and in a time of fire, one does not make calculations and does not behave according to an orderly sequence; one grabs and saves everything one can!

**G.** Furthermore, and essentially:

We are in a situation where "Behold, he is standing behind our wall" — *Moshiach is already standing behind the wall*. Moreover, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said — Hashem has ignited the walls of *galus* ("the Almighty has set the walls of *galus* on fire"). Consequently, the exit from *galus* must be in a manner of *fleeing* ("running away from *galus*"), just as one flees from a fire. At such a time, the hidden powers of the *neshamah* are revealed, in a way that affects even the body! The exodus from Egypt was in a manner of *chafizon* (haste) — "For in haste you left the land of Egypt". And if from Egypt we had to leave in haste, then from this last *galus*, which is much harder and longer, we must certainly leave *in haste*.

And since we must leave and flee from *galus* in haste, it is impossible to make calculations — neither regarding prioritizing *avodah* with oneself over *avodah* with others, nor regarding the order of priority in *avodah* with others. One must flee from *galus* with everything one can save.

And through *avodah* in a manner of haste, we arrive at the future Redemption, regarding which it is said, "For you shall not go out in haste, nor shall you go in flight."

**H.** The Rebbe, my father-in-law, told me that once, on a Shabbos after Pesach, his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), called him and instructed him to take a *Gemara* from the Vilna Shas and study *Pirkei Avos* from it — in accordance with the custom to study *Pirkei Avos* on the Shabbosos between Pesach and Atzeres.

— It should be noted that, apparently, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was accustomed to studying *Pirkei Avos* (not only on the Shabbosos between Pesach and Atzeres, but also) on all the Shabbosos of the summer.

[Usually, it is customary among *Chassidim* to study *Pirkei Avos* only on the Shabbosos between Pesach and Atzeres. — (The Rebbe smiled and said:) They would wait impatiently for the conclusion of the recitation of *Pirkei Avos* in order to repeat a *maamar Chassidus* at *Seudah Shlishis*... But, as mentioned, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was accustomed to saying *Pirkei Avos* on all the Shabbosos of the summer.]

As we find several *maamarim* of *Chassidus* from the Shabbosos after Shavuos beginning "Moshe received Torah from Sinai," "Rabbi says," and the like.

Accordingly, we must explain the lesson and instruction from the beginning of the study of *Pirkei Avos* on this Shabbos — "Moshe received Torah from Sinai, etc.," and as a preface to this: "All of Yisrael have a share in the World to Come," as follows.

**I.** In the *Mishnah* "All of Yisrael have a share in the World to Come" — there is a lesson and instruction regarding the general *avodah* with others:

When speaking with a Jew about the need to engage with others, he might argue: Why should I dedicate my time to others? It is better that I utilize my time for Torah study. The essence of the answer is that *avodah* with others in this world *will bring him benefit* for the World to Come.

The explanation:

One of the differences between this world and the World to Come is that this world is an "inverted world," whereas the World to Come is a "clear world".

Since this is so, it is possible that here in this world ("inverted world"), it seems to him that his virtue is greater than his fellow's, which is why he makes calculations that engaging with his fellow is not worthwhile for him. Whereas in the World to Come ("clear world"), it will be clarified to the contrary.

It is impossible to know who is greater than whom. It is possible that the other is higher than him.

Regarding the other — one must *always* judge him to the scale of merit. Whereas regarding oneself — one cannot rely on the fact that it seems to him that his situation is as it should be, for "love covers all transgressions", love of oneself, and our Sages said, "Do not believe in yourself, etc."

Thus, regarding all those with whom he engages — they *certainly* have a share in the World to Come, whereas regarding himself, a question can arise, etc.

Since this is so, it is possible that as a result of engaging in the welfare of his fellow to bring him closer to Torah and *mitzvos*, his fellow will repay him "in the World to Come," that in the merit of his fellow, he (the *mashpia*) will also merit the World to Come:

When a Jew brings his fellow closer to Torah and *mitzvos*, he becomes his "*Rebbe*," who taught him Torah and brought him to the life of the World to Come.

And through this, the student will repay his Rebbe — that when he comes to the World to Come, *he will not allow* that he (the student) should be in *Gan Eden*, while his "Rebbe" (who taught him Torah and brought him to the life of the World to Come) should be in *Gehinnom*, *chas v'shalom*!

When he comes to the World to Come — he will certainly argue: I cannot be without my Rebbe... So because of his arguments, they will take his "Rebbe" out of *Gehinnom* and seat him in *Gan Eden*!

It should be added that in these days, the repayment of his fellow can be in a way that one does not have to wait until after one hundred and twenty years, "in the World to Come" — for "Behold, he is standing behind our wall," *Moshiach* is about to come *immediately* ("Moshiach is about to come"), "I wait for him every day that he will come," and even the oldest (and certainly the intermediate and the young) in the group will merit the coming of *Moshiach* in his days, so that the benefit his fellow will return to him can be in this world as well ("in *this* world").

**J.** And when one begins to engage with others (after the preface of recognizing that "All of Yisrael have a share in the World to Come") — one must remember that "Moshe received Torah from Sinai and delivered it, etc.":

When engaging with others, one must be careful not to think that "My power and the strength of my hand have made me this wealth".

One must know that engaging with others is only through the power and responsibility of the *Rebbe*, "on the Rebbe's shoulders," and as mentioned above (Section 6) that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, bequeathed to us the power that even in "Egypt" we can engage in spreading Torah and Yiddishkeit (similar to the *avodah* of Yosef HaTzaddik), and we are not doing (and we are forbidden to do) it alone, "on our own shoulders"...

And this is "Moshe received Torah from Sinai and delivered it, etc." — that the *avodah* with others is through the power of Moshe, who "was a lover of Yisrael", and "delivered it to Yehoshua, and Yehoshua to the Elders, and the Elders to the Prophets, etc.," down to our Rebbes in every generation, the extension of Moshe in every generation.

[The Rebbe instructed to play the *nigun* of three movements — of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and the Alter Rebbe.]

**K.** [During the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe instructed several people to say "L'chaim" several times, and he himself also took a lot of *mashke*, and continued to *farbreng* with those seated, addressing individuals specifically, rebuking them, awakening them, and encouraging them to strengthen themselves in their *avodah* in the ways of *Chassidus*, etc., each according to his capacity. — What follows is a "little here and a little there" from the things said during the continuation of the *farbrengen*.

At the beginning of his remarks, the Rebbe said that the *farbrengen* is dragging on and the hour is already late ("it is already a quarter past three"), and people are already starting to think about what the "housewife" will say about the delay of the Shabbos meal... And therefore, one must "grab" before it is too late.

In the continuation of his remarks, the Rebbe awakened and demanded that one must go out of the limitations, "go out of oneself," each according to his situation. For example:]

To one of the *baalei-batim*, he said that he should stop fearing that his tie or hat might not be exactly in place, and his external appearance might not be to the liking of the "housewife"...

[Likewise, he instructed several people to turn their hats, and he himself also turned his hat, saying that even though the "maskilim" (naming some of those present at the *farbrengen*) might think and ask "What is this," one must do it out of *kabbalas-ol*...].

To one of the *baalei-batim* who was wearing a short suit, he said that he is surprised to see him in such attire on Shabbos, and from now on he should start wearing a long garment on Shabbos, as is the custom of *Chassidim*, regardless of his attire on weekdays when he goes to his business, for one must remember the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, that the matter of *galus* is only regarding the body, and not regarding the *neshamah*!

To one of the *baalei-batim* who was not growing his beard, he said that he indeed succeeded in influencing his household in the ways of *Chassidus*, but on himself he has not yet succeeded in influencing... And he continued to speak to him about the greatness of the virtue of growing a beard (not only during *Yemei HaSefirah*...) — which is connected to the thirteen *tikkunim* of the beard, the thirteen attributes of mercy hinted at in the verse, "And He is merciful, He will forgive, etc." And therefore, by growing the beard, all matters are drawn down in the attribute of mercy, even to the drawing down of mercy from the aspect of "He" ("And He is merciful"), a term of concealment, which points to the essential concealment.

And he concluded: You are a "man of business," so listen to my advice and promise me ("tell me yes") that you will grow your beard, and then you will see success in all matters, and you will also be able to add in help and support to educational institutions, etc.

**L.** The Rebbe continued to speak about "going out of oneself" also in matters of *avodah* in Torah and *mitzvos*. For example:

To one of the *baalei-batim*, a *baal-tzedakah*, he said that even when he gives much *tzedakah*, to the point that it seems to him that he gave more than his ability [he made a calculation that he could and should give *tzedakah* in a three-digit amount, and in practice he gave *tzedakah* in a four-digit amount...], he should not be satisfied with that, and certainly not stand in front of the "mirror," pat his belly and say "My insides rejoice"... — although it is understood and simple that even in such a situation (that he feels his virtue in giving *tzedakah*), he must continue in giving *tzedakah*, but together with this, he must strive to nullify the feeling of his own virtue, and know that as much as one does, one can always add and do more.

To one of the *Roshei Yeshivah*, he said that sometimes one must forget that he is a *Rosh Yeshivah* in *Nigleh*, and study *Chassidus* before *davening*, and through this he will influence the students regarding Torah study with fear of Heaven.

To one of the Rabbis, he said that he must repeat *maamarim* of *Chassidus* in his synagogue even if the *baalei-batim* do not want to hear words of *Chassidus*, and he said: In the first few weeks, do not tell them that the things being said are words of *Chassidus*, and then they will hear the things, and after a period of time, when you see that the things found favor in their eyes, you will reveal to them that the things you said are words of *Chassidus*, and then they will no longer care.

— This is how the *bochurim* in Warsaw behaved when they began to distribute the *Chassidus* booklets of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, among the yeshivah students: In the first period, they would publish the *Chassidus* *maamarim* without a "title page," so that they would not know that it is a *Chassidus* *maamar*, and consequently they would examine and study it, thinking that it is a booklet of words of *mussar* and the like, and when they studied, it found favor in their eyes, and then it was possible to reveal to them the "secret" — that it is a *Chassidus* *maamar*!

He also spoke to some of the *bochurim* about matters of conduct in the ways of *Chassidus*, and instructed one that his conduct is in a manner above order and degree, and he is succeeding, with the help of Hashem. And to one he said that he should not be satisfied with the fact that he behaves in the ways of *Chassidus*, but should also influence others, etc.

He also said to some of the *baalei-batim* that they should learn from the *bochurim*, saying: "The reward of all is the pressure". Go and press among the *bochurim*...

He also said: One must also bring the small children, three years old, to push among *Chassidim*...

(And he added with a smile:) One of the *Chassidim* told about a Jew who brought his young son to the "Siyum" on Erev Pesach, and when someone asked him: Does the child understand? He answered him: And they — the adults — do they understand?!...

**M.** The Rebbe continued to demand also from the elder *Chassidim* to "go out of oneself," saying:

Even one who thinks (and even if it is true) that he is in perfection, "he is already a finished one" — even "vessels finished in purity need immersion for the sake of holiness".

The matter in this:

"Kli" (vessel) — an acronym for *Kohanim*, *Leviim*, and *Yisraelim*, which includes all types of Bnei Yisrael and the divisions of their *avodah*. And all of them, even after they reach the perfection of their *avodah*, in the aspect of "vessel finished in purity," in relation to a higher level, "holiness," "need immersion," the letters of *bitul* (nullification).

And since this is so, everyone must go out of the measurements and limitations — "go out of oneself."

In continuation of this, the Rebbe spoke about the matter of *mesiras nefesh*, and mentioned those who gave their lives for *Kiddush Hashem*, saying that it is known that the *Beis Yosef* was distressed that he did not merit to give his life for *Kiddush Hashem*, from which is understood the greatness of the elevation that is achieved by *mesiras nefesh* in practice.

The Rebbe said that they should continue to say "L'chaim," and told:

Once, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, asked his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), to say *Chassidus*, and he answered him that he would say *Chassidus* on the condition that he (the Rebbe, my father-in-law) first drink a cup of *mashke* ("a glass of *arack*"). What did the Rebbe, my father-in-law, do — he drank the cup of *mashke*, and afterwards stuck his finger in his mouth and vomited the drink, so that he could hear the *maamar Chassidus*...

**N.** The Rebbe spoke about the journey for *shlichus* to engage in spreading Yiddishkeit and the wellsprings, and demanded from several *avreichim* that they travel on *shlichus*.

To one who said that he does not know the language of the country, he said: Regarding worldly matters — you manage well with the language of the country... so this is not a hindrance to traveling on *shlichus*.

He awakened one of the *shadarim* about the greatness of the virtue in his *avodah*, saying: When you travel for matters of the *Maamad*, *Atzmus u'Mahus Ein Sof Baruch Hu* travels with you!

And since this is so, one certainly should not be impressed by the fact that sometimes one must remain for Shabbos far from home, because, what is the pain of distance from home compared to the greatness of the virtue in engaging in matters of the *Maamad*.

And he added: Your *avodah* is not only regarding physicality, but to sow spirituality and reap physicality.

When you come to a city, you must inquire and strive regarding matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah and its *mitzvos*, *tefillin*, Shabbos, and the like, and first of all — regarding family purity, for even going to the *mikveh* one time can be a matter that relates to the birth of the child (that it should not be a flawed child, *chas v'shalom*), which is a matter that relates to generations.

He also spoke with one of the activists in the Holy Land, that his work in activism for the benefit of the institutions of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, must be with *strength*, and then his words will be accepted and will have their effect.

**O.** During the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe gave blessings to several people regarding their private matters.

To one who asked for a blessing for his brother that he should merit to leave the valley of tears, saying that he wants to receive a blessing like so-and-so received regarding this matter — the Rebbe answered: I am therefore forced not to be impressed and to reveal to you the truth — that giving a blessing is a matter that relates to and depends on the root of the *neshamah*...

At the *farbrengen*, a Jew was present who participated in "chess" competitions, who had begun to draw closer to Yiddishkeit, and the Rebbe said to him that if he accepts upon himself to continue and add in matters of Yiddishkeit, then he will bless him that he should succeed in the games, and told:

In his youth, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, once played with the *Chossid* R' Elchanan Dov, and when the Rebbe (Rashab) noticed them, he intervened in their game, and suggested to them ideas how to continue their moves in the game, and explained the content of the things in the *avodah* of Hashem.

(And the Rebbe concluded:) With the Rebbe (Rashab), it was in a manner *from above to below*, that from the details of the matters in spiritual *avodah* he understood and knew the details of the matters in the game in physicality. With you — it should be at least in a manner *from below to above*, to elevate the matters of the world and make them vessels for *Elokus*.

**P.** (To the *gabbai*, the *Chossid* R' Yochanan Gordon, he said:) You merited to be a *gabbai* in the synagogue and *beis medrash* of Lubavitch that is in Lubavitch, that even though it is for the time being in New York, "the synagogues and *batei medrash* that are in Bavel are destined to be established in the Land of Yisrael," as it is in the *Gemara*.

[The Rebbe asked to examine the language of the *Gemara*, and after the examination, he continued to speak about other matters while holding the *Gemara* in his holy hands, and when one of the *Chassidim* suggested taking the *Gemara*, saying "perhaps it is heavy for the Rebbe," the Rebbe said: "For a Rebbe, Torah is not heavy."]

**Q.** [When the time of the *farbrengen* dragged on, one of the elder *Chassidim* asked to end the *farbrengen* for the benefit of the Rebbe's health, and the Rebbe answered him with a smile: At the time of saying the *maamar*, you stood in a corner, and now you come to give opinions?!... And here his holy face became serious, and he began to speak about the matter of *nesi'us*, saying:]

When one contemplates the greatness of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, and the fact that he left us...

— I do not know why Hashem did so, but, such is the situation in practice, and it is clear that this is not against his will, for with the Rebbe, the concept of "against his will" does not apply. And when the Rebbe agrees to a certain matter, it is because that is his will —

There is no other choice for you, and there is no other choice for me either...

And in any case, regarding the matters that I took upon myself, which is my *shlichus* in this world, I strive that they should be in kindness and mercy...

In the continuation of the remarks, when one of the *Chassidim* mentioned the Rebbe Rayatz with the title "the Rebbe, of blessed memory" — the Rebbe protested, saying (with great emotion and weeping):

Why are you "sending away" ("farsheikt") the Rebbe, my father-in-law, to "Siberia," to "Solovki"... to *Gan Eden*?! — We need him (and perhaps he also needs us) *here*!...

Even if for this purpose we must *take him out* of *Gan Eden*, the lower *Gan Eden*, and even the upper *Gan Eden* — *it is worth it*, because the elevation of *Gan Eden* (even the upper *Gan Eden*) is only lights and revelations, whereas in this world — when one says *L'chaim* on *mashke* and eats physical food — there is *Atzmus u'Mahus Ein Sof Baruch Hu*...

(And the Rebbe concluded — hitting his fist on the table:) We need the Rebbe — together with all the Rebbes — here.

**R.** The Rebbe instructed to play the *nigun* of three movements — of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and the Alter Rebbe, and they played it many times. Once, he stopped at the third movement (of the Alter Rebbe) and instructed to repeat this movement, saying:

The third movement, of the Alter Rebbe, is the one that relates to us the most, because the Alter Rebbe was a new *neshamah*, through whom a new drawing down from *Atzmus u'Mahus Ein Sof Baruch Hu* is made, and through him it is also drawn down to his generations.

And afterwards he said:

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, said about *Moshiach*: "Behold, he is standing behind our wall, watching through the windows, peering through the lattices". (And he pointed with his holy hand at the wall, and said:) "He is standing behind the wall," and looks at us through the window, and wonders why we are delaying his coming!...

**S.** [Before *davening* *Ma'ariv*, the Rebbe instructed to play the *nigun* of three movements, and after *davening* *Ma'ariv*, he instructed to play it again. And afterwards he said:]

Since

## 11 Iyar 5712. Tuesday, Parshas Emor.

- To the activists of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, in the Rebbe’s study -
(Unedited)

1. [After various suggestions were raised regarding the yeshiva’s financial crisis, the Rebbe remarked: I am not an expert in fundraising, and then said:]

All the suggestions raised here are suggestions that can and should be utilized even in a regular, normal situation. However, since we are dealing with an emergency situation, the means to improve and rectify the situation must also be commensurate with that.

First and foremost, when discussing the crisis in the yeshiva’s financial state, one must also utilize the positive side of the crisis.

One must also pay attention to the spiritual crisis currently prevailing in the lives of Bnei Yisrael—a result of the general situation in the world, which has caused a general spiritual revolution and a mood that is conducive to drawing the hearts of Jewish sons and daughters toward Torah and Yiddishkeit.

In recent years, due to the wars and unrest in the world, we have seen tangibly that matters and values that were considered eternal have withered and vanished. Opinions and beliefs have been disappointed. Countries that championed the name of science and investigation have not only failed to bring justice and righteousness, but on the contrary, have led to murder, and so on.

All this has brought the youth to a great spiritual agitation, which has naturally caused a soulful yearning for truth. This is true regarding youth in general, and Jewish youth in particular, for Bnei Yisrael are "believers, the children of believers".

The world revolution of recent years has introduced restlessness and yearnings into the hearts of Jewish youth—yearnings for a Torah and Yiddishkeit full of content, for it is only in Torah and practical mitzvos that the souls of Yisrael find content and rectification. It turns out, therefore, that in these days, the yeshivos occupy an extremely important and unique place, and bear a great responsibility the likes of which has never been seen before.

There is now an opportunity and possibility to accomplish much in the field of Torah and Yiddishkeit with relatively light efforts. One must not miss the hour and lose the opportunity, for it is a loss that cannot be recovered.

2. The role of the yeshivos in general, and Lubavitch yeshivos in particular, wherever they may be, is not only to raise a generation of G-d-fearing and complete individuals, talmidei chachamim, but also to plant in their hearts a sense of responsibility and mesiras nefesh to act and work for the benefit of the environment in which they find themselves. This role is being fulfilled with great success, thank G-d, in the Lubavitch yeshivos, where the students are educated, while still within the walls of the yeshiva, to be educational activists and active in the dissemination of Torah and Yiddishkeit.

The role of the yeshiva students is not only to study Torah for themselves and work on refining their own character traits, but also to influence their environment and prepare themselves for devoted public work in disseminating Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit, to be carriers of the banner of Torah in all their future places of residence.

In accordance with the intent of the great founder of the Lubavitch yeshivos 55 years ago, the students of Lubavitch yeshivos, wherever they are, are "candles to illuminate"—not only their environment, but candles lighting candles, one candle from another, to illuminate with the light of Torah, mitzvos, and the pnimiyus haTorah.

3. The role of the yeshiva activists and all those who take part in public work is not only to worry about the material state of the yeshivos, but also to ensure that the number of their students continues to grow and increase, so that all seekers of truth among the Jewish youth can find their solution in the yeshiva.

You, the baalei-batim who are involved in supporting the yeshivos and proper education in general—upon you now rests the privilege and the duty to act even more for the support of yeshivos in general, and for the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch yeshivos in particular.

You must act to solicit contributions from additional Jews for the benefit of the yeshivos, especially since this action itself constitutes an opportunity to add new students to the yeshivos—as per the words of the Rebbe, that the greatness of the action of soliciting Jews for the support of Torah is not only that they give from their money for the support of Torah, but also that through this, they and their family members are also drawn closer to a life of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos.

4. In light of the grave situation currently prevailing in the yeshiva, one must find the appropriate advice and take the necessary measures immediately, as soon as possible. For when one procrastinates and continues on with the regular measures, one may, G-d forbid, reach a state where the regular measures will no longer be of any help, and then the path to rectifying the situation will be harder and longer, and sometimes it will even be too late, G-d forbid.

Therefore, in addition to the need and necessity to continue with all the regular measures and strengthen them as much as possible, it is my opinion and suggestion that the activists present here decide immediately on holding a *special event* in which many baalei-batim will participate, with each of you making an effort to influence your friends and acquaintances to come and participate in this event, where they will donate from their money for the benefit of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch yeshivos.

One should not be satisfied with a mere meeting, "hungerdig" (in a hungry manner)... but as Chazal say, "Great is the meal (the food one feeds guests) that brings [people] closer," and as is seen tangibly, that during eating or drinking (or both together), it is easier for a baal-habayis to write a check... Therefore, it is appropriate that the aforementioned event take place within the framework of a *meal*—breakfast, lunch, or supper.

And because of the great necessity for speed in this matter, the event must take place in the coming weeks, and a precise date must be set now for when this event will take place.

5. And it would be best if the start of the action in this regard would be at the current meeting, through "pledges":

Each of the activists present will commit to donating a certain sum of money (from his own money or from money he will collect for this purpose from his friends and acquaintances), for the very decision regarding this in the presence of several tens of Yisrael will constitute an addition of *giving strength* to carry out the decision *in actual practice*.

This is similar to what Chazal say, "They take an oath to fulfill the mitzvah"—that even though one has already been commanded by the Ribono shel Olam to fulfill the mitzvah, and "is already sworn from *Har Sinai*," and if so, what is the benefit of his oath to fulfill the mitzvah? Nevertheless, when one accepts it upon himself once more, this acts as an addition of strength to fulfill the matter, and furthermore, through this, new means are opened up for him ("es machen zich naye vegen") through which he can fulfill the matter.

I have known for a long time, and also from this meeting, that you have already done much for the benefit of the Lubavitch yeshivos; however, pledging a certain sum in the presence of several minyanim of Bnei Yisrael will grant you new strengths to find new means through which you will be able to fulfill the pledge.

6. Regarding the suggestion raised earlier by one of the activists to organize a large raffle among all the donors for the benefit of the yeshivos—this is, in essence, a fair suggestion ("a gleiche zach"), but it is not relevant for the activists present here, because (in addition to the fact that the matter involves large expenses) in order to realize a plan such as this, the activists would need to visit *hundreds* of people and speak *hundreds* of times about "Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch," until they become sick of it... and in the end, they would succeed in receiving only one dollar, and sometimes it is even possible that after all the talking and time, the matter would end with a number "zero" on the left side ("a zero fun der linker zeit")!

The realization of this plan should therefore be handed over to the "rank and file," that is, to the bochurim, the beggars... but in my opinion, it is not at all suitable for wealthy individuals.

What should be done in my opinion is, as mentioned, to decide on holding a special event for the benefit of the yeshiva as soon as possible, and to begin with a financial pledge from each of those present, and they will also influence their friends and acquaintances to participate in the aforementioned.

This, then, is my opinion—as someone who is not an expert in this field, and everyone is free to express their opinion on this.

7. [After all those gathered expressed their agreement with the Rebbe’s suggestion, he said:]

I would like to add—in connection with what was mentioned about the lack of publicity—that since there are also representatives of the press present here, it is worthwhile that they be given (as soon as possible, since time is short) the details of the matter, with an appropriate "headline," etc., so that they do their part in publicizing the aforementioned plan.

And also—according to the "custom" at every meeting to immediately schedule a second meeting—it is appropriate that they decide to organize an additional, smaller meeting to consolidate the details of the plans regarding the aforementioned event, and also to summarize additional suggestions that have not yet been finalized.

(And the Rebbe concluded):

I would like to express my gratitude to you for your participation in the meeting, although I think it is unnecessary, since all those present here are Jews who are devoted to the benefit of the yeshivos.

And like every living thing that needs to grow and develop—may the Ribono shel Olam help that we have the possibility to continue and increase and strengthen our work in supporting the yeshivos and in disseminating Torah in general, and in the language of Chazal—"we elevate in matters of holiness."

I wish you all a happy Shavuos and the receiving of the Torah with joy.

## Sicha of 19 Iyar - 34th Day of the Omer - 5712

Creation is a descent and a *Seder Hishtalshelus* from above to below. The intent, however, is that there subsequently be an ascent after ascent from below to above. Since this is the supreme intent, it is indeed brought about in actuality. From the moment the descent was completed, the ascent after ascent began. In a revealed manner, this is seen in the *neshamos* in *Gan Eden*. And regarding *tzaddikim*, this is true even in this world, as our Sages have stated that *talmidei chachamim* have no rest, neither in this world nor in the World to Come, for they go from strength to strength.

Even though throughout the six thousand years there are various changes in ascents and descents, the verse states, "A *tzaddik* falls seven times and rises," meaning the fall is for the sake of the rising and the ascent that follows. This fall and descent is necessary, as is explained at length in many places, that between a previous level and a more elevated level that follows, there must be a *bitul* in between. This is also the case in the order of descent from above to below: between one existence and another, there must be an *ayin* (nothingness) in between.

This is what the Baal Shem Tov meant when he said that even though he could ascend to heaven in a whirlwind, like Eliyahu the Prophet, he preferred to undergo the process of "to dust you shall return". This is because the lowest descent—"to dust you shall return"—is a preparation for a level even higher than an ascent in a whirlwind.

Since this preparatory descent is necessary for an ascent to a higher level, it is, in truth, not a descent at all, but rather a part of the higher ascent itself.

This is the general concept of passing away and mourning: Regarding the one who has passed away, the passing is the matter of "to dust you shall return" for the sake of the higher ascent that follows. Regarding the mourners—may they be separated for a good life—the matter of mourning, which is *mochin d'katnus*, is also for the sake of an ascent to a higher level that follows.

It can be said that this is also the content hinted at in the language of consolation, that we include the mourner among the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim. For the level of Moshiach and the Third *Beis Hamikdash* are much higher than the level that existed before the destruction. Moshiach was born at the very moment of the destruction, as is recounted in *Eicha Rabbah*, meaning that immediately upon the lowest descent (but not before it), the *Geulah* began.

However, a person requires great exertion and *avodah* until he reaches such a level that, at the time of a fall or descent, he feels in actuality—and does not merely believe or understand—that it is nothing but a necessary preparation for an ascent to the highest level. This must also be the intent of those who offer consolation, for only through this is it possible to be truly comforted, among the rest of the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Bamidbar, Mevarchim HaChodesh and Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

Five acquisitions did the Ribono shel Olam acquire in His world: Torah is one acquisition, Avraham is one acquisition, heaven and earth are one acquisition, Yisrael is one acquisition, and the Beis HaMikdash is one acquisition. The simple interpretation of this statement of our Sages is that there are five things in the world that are precious to the Ribono shel Olam, and therefore they are called an "acquisition" — a term that denotes the importance of an object to a person, such that they would pay money for it, with which they could have purchased the life of their soul. These five things are listed according to their chronological order. It begins with Torah, as our Sages say, "Two thousand years before the world, Torah preceded it," followed by heaven and earth, which is the world itself, and then Avraham, Yisrael, and the Beis HaMikdash, corresponding to the chronological order.

We must understand: seemingly, according to the simple interpretation, it should have said, "The Ribono shel Olam has five acquisitions," to indicate their importance. Why does it say, "Five acquisitions did the Ribono shel Olam acquire," which implies that they are acquisitions not because of their own nature, but because of the act of acquisition that the Ribono shel Olam performed upon them? Furthermore, we must understand why it says, "Five acquisitions... in His world," as the word "in His world" seems superfluous. Most puzzling of all: since it lists heaven and earth among them—which are the totality of the world, for there is nothing in the world that is not included in heaven and earth—what is the meaning of saying that "in His world" He acquired heaven and earth? Also, why the precision of "in *His* world" (and not just "in the world")? Seemingly, even without this, it is understood that the world is the world of the Ribono shel Olam; why then is it necessary to specifically add "in His world"?

2) The matter is this: the five acquisitions that the Ribono shel Olam acquired are specifically "in His world"—meaning, a world that provides no room for the mistake that it is an independent domain, two domains G-d forbid, "divided above... divided below", but rather a world in which it is recognizable that it is the world of the Ribono shel Olam. In order for these matters to be elevated to become "in His world," there must be an act of acquisition performed upon them; this is the meaning of "the Ribono shel Olam acquired in His world."

To explain: an acquisition is not the creation of something new, but rather the transition of an object from the domain of the seller to the domain of the buyer—the object was initially in the seller's domain, and through the acquisition, it comes to be revealed in the buyer's domain. This has a parallel above: an "acquisition" indicates that this is not a new creation, *yesh me'ayin*, but rather that it comes from concealment into revelation alone. This refers generally to the world of Atzilus, as is known regarding the interpretation of "Blessed is your Possessor (*Konecha*), blessed is your Creator (*Borecha*), blessed is your Former (*Yotzrecha*), blessed is your Maker (*Osecha*)". "Creator," "Former," and "Maker" correspond to the three worlds of Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah—meaning, the matter of creation *yesh me'ayin* begins from the world of Beriah, where the possibility of existence begins, and through the proliferation of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, it can lead to the possibility of the mistake that there are two domains, G-d forbid. Not so the world of Atzilus, which is called an "acquisition" (*kinyan*); hence it says, "Blessed is your Possessor (*Konecha*)." Since it is not the creation of something new, *yesh me'ayin*, but only the revelation of what was concealed, and since the world of Atzilus is an intermediary between the *Ma'atzil* (the Emanator) and the created beings—meaning, it conveys and draws down from the *Ma'atzil* to the created beings—it is understood that there is no creation of anything new, only that the matters which were concealed in the *Ma'atzil* are drawn down and come into revelation. And since the world of Atzilus is not the creation of something new, but only the revelation of the concealed, there is no room for the mistake of [two domains], for in the world of Atzilus it is written, "No evil shall dwell with You," and it is clearly recognizable that it is His (the Ribono shel Olam's) world, for in the world of Atzilus, "He and His life are one, He and His attributes are one".

In addition to this, there is also the act of acquisition that the Ribono shel Olam performs in the world below, through which even the matters of the world below are elevated to become "in His world." This is the meaning of "Five acquisitions did the Ribono shel Olam acquire in His world"—that in order for these matters (which are found in the world below) to be elevated to become "in His world," there must be an act of acquisition performed upon them: "the Ribono shel Olam acquired."

3) This can be understood from the concept of acquisition below, through which an object comes from the domain of the seller to the domain of the buyer. There are two modes of acquisition: *meshichah* (pulling) and *kesef* (money). On this, Reish Lakish and Rabbi Yochanan disagree: Reish Lakish holds that *meshichah* is explicitly from the Torah—when the buyer pulls the object into his domain, it becomes his, and thereby the buyer becomes obligated to give money to the seller. Rabbi Yochanan holds that by Torah law, money effects the acquisition—that even by giving the money, he has acquired the object—yet the Sages decreed that *meshichah* is required, and he does not acquire the object until he pulls it into his domain. The difference between them is that in *meshichah*, the act of acquisition consists of demonstrating that the object has entered his domain (which is why *meshichah* is only effective in a private domain or an alleyway, unlike a public domain), and thereby the buyer becomes obligated to pay the seller as they agreed. Conversely, in *kesef*, the act of acquisition is such that no change is made to the object itself, and therefore the Sages decreed that he does not acquire it until he pulls the object, as this demonstrates that it has entered his domain.

The same applies to the concept of acquisition in spirituality. Regarding all matters of the world, it is written, "Which G-d created to do," to rectify—that everything created in the world requires rectification. This means that from the perspective of creation, it is in a state of lacking perfection, and from this it is understood that it is not in the domain of holiness, the domain of the Ribono shel Olam. Since "He is the perfection of all", anything that is not in perfection is not in the domain of the Ribono shel Olam, so to speak—the domain of holiness. Therefore, there must be the *avodah* to effect the acquisition of the Ribono shel Olam, so that all matters of the world are elevated to the domain of the Ribono shel Olam, the "private domain of the Unique One of the world", which refers to the world of Atzilus, called "His world" (as mentioned in section 2).

In this acquisition, there are two modes: *meshichah* and *kesef*. *Meshichah* refers to the elevation of all the matters of man and the world, which are drawn and ascend to the domain of holiness through the totality of man's *avodah* in the manner of *is'arusa d'letata* (awakening from below). *Kesef* (money), from the expression "I have greatly longed (*nichsof nichsafti*)", refers to the love that is drawn from above in the manner of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (awakening from above). Within this itself, there are two modes, similar to the two modes in the acquisition of money in its literal sense: whether the acquisition is effected by the money (by Torah law, money effects acquisition) and afterwards comes the *meshichah*, or whether the money is given after the acquisition is effected by the *meshichah*. Their parallels in spiritual *kesef*—which refers to the drawing down from above—are: *is'arusa d'le'eila* that precedes and brings about *is'arusa d'letata* (money before *meshichah*), and *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes after and through *is'arusa d'letata* (money after *meshichah*).

The matter is that in love (*kesef*) itself, there are two levels: *ahavah zuta* (lesser love) and *ahavah rabbah* (great love). *Ahavah zuta* is the love that is based on reason and intellect—one contemplates that Elokus is a good thing, and through this, love is born in his heart. This love is measured and limited, for since it is born through intellectual grasp, it is limited by the intellect that gives birth to it; furthermore, the intellectual grasp is only of the level of Elokus that is enclothed in the worlds, which is in a state of measurement and limitation. Therefore, the concept of *kilos hanefesh* (longing of the soul)—which is a matter that transcends measurement and limitation—does not apply to it. Moreover, this love is born through the contemplation that Elokus is good *for him*, as it is written, "For He is your life," and consequently, the concept of *kilos hanefesh*, which is a matter that transcends one's own existence, does not apply.

*Ahavah rabbah* is a love that transcends reason and intellect, which is drawn from above. That is, after the completion of his *avodah* to the extent of his ability with love based on reason and intellect, he then reaches *ahavah rabbah*, which transcends reason and intellect. It is drawn from above due to the essential love of the Ribono shel Olam for the Jewish people, and through it, the hidden love that is in the nature of all Jews from their birth is awakened in the heart of man—a love that transcends reason and intellect, and transcends measurement and limitation. [In this love itself, there are two modes: love like "flames of fire," in the manner of thirst from below to above, and love in "delights," which is from above to below]. The two levels of love (*ahavah zuta* and *ahavah rabbah*) are connected to the two modes of *kesef* (*is'arusa d'le'eila* that precedes *is'arusa d'letata*, and *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes after *is'arusa d'letata*). For the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that precedes *is'arusa d'letata* (money before *meshichah*) effects the *avodah* of man to arrive at love through contemplation in his intellect, which is *ahavah zuta*; and through the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes after *is'arusa d'letata* (money after *meshichah*), comes the love that transcends reason and intellect, *ahavah rabbah*.

4) Now, among the acquisitions that the Ribono shel Olam acquired in His world, it lists first "Torah is one acquisition," and it was explained above (section 1) that this is because "Two thousand years before the world, Torah preceded it." The matter is that the creation of the world is from the aspect of the *Midos* (attributes), as it is written, "Remember Your mercies and Your kindnesses, for they are from of old (*me'olam*)," and it is written, "For I said, the world (*olam*) shall be built with kindness." Torah, however, is from the aspect of the *Mochin* (intellect), and therefore it preceded the world. This is the meaning of the statement, "Five acquisitions did the Ribono shel Olam acquire in His world: Torah is one acquisition"—that one must draw Torah, which is from the aspect of the *Mochin* (the three first *Sefiros*), into the world, whose creation is from the aspect of the *Midos*. Through this, the acquisition is effected: the world is elevated to the "private domain," to become "His (the Ribono shel Olam's) world." This is also why it continues, "Heaven and earth are one acquisition"—that through the Torah, the acquisition is also effected in heaven and earth, which are elevated to the "private domain" to become "His (the Ribono shel Olam's) world."

There is another aspect to "Torah is one acquisition": that Torah itself is one of the five acquisitions in the world whose creation is from the aspect of the *Midos*—meaning, the five acquisitions include the totality of the *Midos*. Avraham is the aspect of *Chesed*, as it is written, "Avraham My beloved." Torah is the aspect of *Gevurah*, as it is written at the beginning of the Ten Commandments, "And G-d spoke (*Vayedaber Elokim*)..." specifically, and so it is in the language of our Sages, "I am... and You shall have no... from the mouth of the *Gevurah* we heard them"—*Gevurah* specifically. Yisrael, in addition to referring to *Ze'er Anpin* (the totality of the *Midos*), refers to the aspect of *Tiferes*, the middle line that includes *Chesed* and *Gevurah*. Heaven and earth refer to the aspect of *Yesod*, as it is written, "For all that is in heaven and in earth," which "grasps heaven and earth", which is the aspect of *Yesod*. The Beis HaMikdash is the aspect of *Malchus*, as it is written, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary and I will dwell among them (*b'tocham*)," the language of *Shechinah* specifically, which refers to the aspect of *Malchus* that dwells and enclothes itself in the lower beings.

We can connect the two aforementioned matters regarding the interpretation of "Torah is one acquisition" (that Torah is the aspect of *Mochin* which transcends the world whose creation is from the *Midos*, and that Torah is one of the five acquisitions which correspond to the *Midos*) by first explaining the connection of Torah to the aspect of *Gevurah*. Seemingly, Torah is the aspect of *Chesed*, as it is written, "The Torah of kindness," and also, "Torah emanates from *Chochma*," and *Chochma* is on the right line. But the matter is that Torah being the aspect of *Gevurah* is similar to the concept of the "might (*gevuros*) of rains" (which descend with *Gevurah*). This is not *Tzimtzum* in the sense of judgment (contraction for the sake of contraction), but on the contrary, in the sense of the intensification of vitality. For the primary influence in a proliferation of light and vitality is only through the aspect of *Gevurah* specifically, and the *Tzimtzum* is only a matter of division into drops so that the influence can be received below, as our Sages say, "If two drops were to emerge from one mold, they would blur the earth..." Similarly with Torah: its greatness is immense, for it preceded the world, being the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam, and "Torah and the Holy One, blessed be He, are one". Nevertheless, it is drawn down and comes to the lowest level specifically, as our Sages say, "To Egypt you descended..." Therefore, it is necessary that the drawing down below be in the manner of *Gevurah* (contraction and division). Through this, the Torah effects the acquisition in the world.

5) Now, in addition to what was explained above—that the Torah effects the acquisition in the world—there must also be the act of acquisition in the Torah itself. The matter is that although Torah is the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam and "Torah and the Holy One, blessed be He, are one," it descended to the lowest level, "To Egypt you descended," and became enclothed in physical matters, even to the point of false arguments—if one argues this way and another argues that way—where it is inevitable that one of them is not speaking the truth. Because of the descent of the Torah to the lowest level, it is possible for a person's Torah study to be not as it should be, even to the point of "interpreting the Torah in a way that is not according to the *Halacha*", G-d forbid, in order to provoke, or at the very least, not for its own sake but "in order to be called a Rabbi", and the like. Therefore, there must be an act of acquisition in the study of Torah, to elevate it to the "private domain"—meaning, that the study of Torah should be in such a way that the person studying feels that this is the Torah of the Ribono shel Olam, His wisdom and His will.

This is accomplished by preceding it with the *avodah* of *tefillah*. It is stated in the Gemara, "Abba Binyamin says... regarding my prayer, that it should be adjacent to my bed," and Rashi explains: not to engage in Torah study when I rise from my bed until I recite the *Shema* and pray. The *Tosafos* asks: I do not know from where he derives that it is forbidden to study before prayer. But the matter is that although there is truly no prohibition in studying Torah before prayer, nevertheless, because of the descent of the Torah below, the study can be not as it should be—in order to be called a Rabbi, to provoke, or even interpreting the Torah not according to the *Halacha* (as mentioned above). For this, the *avodah* of *tefillah* must precede it, in the manner of contemplation, etc., "Know before Whom you are standing", until one reaches the *mesiras nefesh* of the *Shema*, and the *bitul* like a servant before his master in the *Shemoneh Esrei* (which is also recognizable and visible externally in the bowing and prostration, etc.). Through this, the state of "To You, Hashem, I lift up my soul" is achieved, to unify it with Your oneness, which is a matter of actual *mesiras nefesh* just as when it departs from the body, that it does not think of the needs of the body. Through this preparation, the acquisition in Torah is effected: that the study of Torah is in the "private domain," in a manner of connection and unification with the Ribono shel Olam.
