Furthermore, in the study of Torah itself (in addition to the *avodah* of *tefillah*), the acquisition is effected by studying the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of the Torah. The descent of the Torah to be enclothed in physical matters, even to the point of false arguments, is only in the *nigleh* (revealed) part of Torah, which is the aspect of the "Tree of Knowledge of Good and Evil". Not so the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, the "secrets of the Torah," which is the aspect of the "Tree of Life". Therefore, through the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, the study of the *nigleh* of the Torah is also done as it should be. Even when studying matters of the Torah that have descended and become enclothed in physical things and even false arguments, not only do the worldly matters in which the Torah has descended and become enclothed not distract him from feeling that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam, but furthermore, through the study of Torah, he effects that the world itself is clarified and elevated to the "private domain." This is the concept of "heaven and earth are one acquisition" that is effected through "Torah is one acquisition" (as mentioned in section 4).

6) We should add regarding the general concept of acquisition: although it was explained above (section 2) that it refers to the ascent to the world of Atzilus—which is the concept of "Blessed is your Possessor"—it truly refers also to the ascent to a level that transcends Atzilus. For the act of acquisition is through the drawing down to the "private domain"—*Yachid* (Unique One) specifically—and the aspect of *Yachid* is higher than Atzilus, for Atzilus is in the aspect of *Echad* (One), which is below *Yachid*. The matter is, as is known, the difference between *Echad* and *Yachid*: *Echad* means that there is a division of details, but through contemplation, one knows that in truth it is *Echad*. *Yachid*, however, is in a manner where there is no division at all. This is also the difference between the world of Atzilus and what is above Atzilus. It is known that there are three levels: *A'kudim*, *Nekudim*, and *Berudim*. *Berudim* refers to the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*, which are in a manner of separation, *alma d'peruda* (even though they also have an aspect of unity). *Nekudim* refers to the world of Atzilus, the world of unity, where "He and His life are one, He and His attributes are one," but nevertheless, there is the matter of the division of "His life" and "His attributes"—the mode of the unification of "He" with "His life" is not the same as the mode of the unification of "He" with "His attributes". In addition, there is also the division of the light into ten *Sefiros* (*Chochma*, etc., *Chesed*, etc.), yet they are in the aspect of *Echad* because it is felt in them that there is one Master for all the *Sefiros*. Above this is *A'kudim*, where all the lights are included in one vessel, without any division at all, which is the concept of *Yachid* that transcends *Echad*. From this, it is understood that the true meaning of acquisition—which is the ascent to the "private domain," *Yachid* that transcends *Echad*—refers to the ascent to a level that transcends Atzilus. This is the true meaning of "heaven and earth are one acquisition": that the ascent of the totality of the world (heaven and earth) should be not only to the level of Atzilus, but also to the level that transcends Atzilus. As is explained elsewhere, the true meaning of "a dwelling place for Him in the lower worlds" is that there should also be the revelation of what transcends Atzilus.

The same applies to "Torah is one acquisition": the concept of acquisition is to elevate the Torah to a level that transcends Atzilus. It is known what is stated in the writings of the AriZal regarding the interpretation of "And Your Torah that You have taught us": "Your Torah" refers to the Torah as it is in Atzilus, and "that You have taught us" refers to the Torah as it is in *Beriah*. Meaning, our Torah is the Torah of *Beriah*, as is hinted at by the fact that the beginning of the Torah is with the letter *Beis*, the acronym for *Beriah*. The meaning of "Torah is one acquisition" is that even our Torah, which is in *Beriah*—and even as it has descended to the lowest level, "To Egypt you descended," etc.—should be elevated above, not only to the level of the world of Atzilus ("Your Torah" in Atzilus), but also to the level that transcends Atzilus. And it is written that David would connect the Torah that is above to the Ribono shel Olam—meaning, that the Torah that is above, "Your Torah" in Atzilus, David would connect to the Ribono shel Olam, the aspect of *Ein Sof* that transcends Atzilus. This was accomplished by David specifically, whose *avodah* was in the manner of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), as our Sages say, "What is the meaning of the verse, 'The utterance of David the son of Yishai, and the utterance of the man raised on high'? The utterance of David the son of Yishai, who established the yoke of *teshuvah*, who accepted upon himself the yoke of Torah and the yoke of *mitzvos*"—*yoke* specifically. This is the concept of *mesiras nefesh* and *bitul* that is in the *avodah* of *tefillah* before the study of Torah (as mentioned in section 5), through which the acquisition of Torah is effected: to elevate the Torah from below and connect it to the Ribono shel Olam, the aspect of *Ein Sof* that transcends Atzilus, the aspect of *Yachid*. The same applies to the other acquisitions, up to "the Beis HaMikdash is one acquisition," which refers to the aspect of *Malchus* (as mentioned in section 4), where the act of acquisition is that the elevation should be not only to the aspect of *Malchus* of Atzilus, but also to the aspect of *Malchus* of *Ein Sof* that transcends Atzilus, the aspect of *Yachid*.

7) This is the content of the entire statement, "Five acquisitions did the Ribono shel Olam acquire in His world." Just as with all matters of Torah—from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—this statement is also (not merely a story, but) an instruction for every single Jew: that in order for the five acquisitions to be "in His (the Ribono shel Olam's) world," there must be the act of acquisition—"the Ribono shel Olam acquired" specifically—which is accomplished through the *avodah* of the Jewish people specifically. As explained above (section 3), all matters as they were created by the Ribono shel Olam are in the manner of "which G-d created to do," to rectify—that it requires rectification, and the rectification depends on the *avodah* of the Jewish people specifically, who through their *avodah* elevate all matters to the "private domain," the aspect of *Yachid* that transcends Atzilus. The power for this is given to every single Jew, as it is stated in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu* that every Jew can say, "When will my deeds reach the deeds of my forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov?" It is in the power of every single Jew to clarify his portion in the world and elevate it to the "private domain," through which the intent is fulfilled that the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds.

## Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Bamidbar, Mevarchim HaChodesh and Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5712

**A. The Rebbe instructed to play a nigun and recited a maamar on the theme of "Five acquisitions the Holy One, Blessed be He, acquired in His world."**
[After the maamar, the Rebbe instructed to say "L’chaim," and afterwards instructed to play the "Nigun of Three Movements" (of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and the Alter Rebbe).]

***

**B.** The significance of Rosh Chodesh Sivan (which includes all the days of the month, similar to the "head" which includes the vitality of all the limbs) — which is included in this Shabbos, Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, "from which all the days are blessed" — is explicitly stated in the verse: "In the third month... on this day (Rosh Chodesh) *they came to the wilderness of Sinai*."

Among the points regarding this:
The Gemara states: "Mount *Sinai*, that hatred for the nations of the world descended upon it."
Its meaning in the *avodah* of man: "The nations of the world" refers to the physicality and materiality of the world, as understood from the words of the Midrash that "Esau (the nations of the world) took 'this world' (physicality and materiality) as his portion, and Jacob took the 'world to come' as his portion"; and "hatred for the nations of the world" means a feeling of hatred for the matters of this world.

This is the innovation of Matan Torah (beginning from Rosh Chodesh Sivan—and consequently also Shabbos Mevarchim, which includes Rosh Chodesh Sivan—due to the preparation for Matan Torah that occurs when "they came to the wilderness of Sinai")—that not only is pleasure ("geshmak") in the matters of this world negated, but furthermore, a feeling of hatred for the matters of this world is created.

**C.** An explanation of this matter:
Torah activates all the *hemshech* (drawings-down of Divine energy), including those regarding physical matters, as explicitly stated in the verse, "If you walk in My statutes," "that you shall be toiling in Torah" (as Rashi explains), then "I will give your rains in their time, etc.," meaning that all *hemshech* in physical matters will be drawn down.

Since this is so, Matan Torah certainly does not negate physical matters; the effect of Matan Torah is only to negate the "geshmak" in physical matters.
On the contrary—through the negation of the "geshmak" in physical matters, a *great increase* is created in the *hemshech* of physical matters themselves:
Physicality in and of itself is a limited thing, whereas when one negates the "geshmak" in physicality, it is for him like a spiritual matter, and consequently, physical matters are drawn down *without limitations*.

**D.** This should be connected with the words of the Mishnah in Pirkei Avos that we study on this Shabbos—"Five acquisitions, etc.: Torah is one acquisition, heaven and earth are one acquisition, etc.":
It was explained above (in the maamar) the meaning of "Torah is one acquisition"—that one effects an "acquisition" in Torah to draw it down and elevate it to the world of Atzilus, and even above Atzilus; and through this, "heaven and earth are also one acquisition"—that one effects a change in the physicality of the world, so that the physicality becomes spirituality and *Elokus*, just like in the world of Atzilus and above Atzilus, such that even below, the light from above Atzilus is felt ("hert zich") in physical things.

—And to note what is explained in *Likutei Torah* that "there exists even below a level of Atzilus" (and similarly the levels above Atzilus), and proof of this is that "the soul of Moshe Rabbeinu was from the level of Atzilus, and likewise the soul of Avraham, meaning that in Moshe Rabbeinu and Avraham, Atzilus shone in them in a state of revelation below" (and similarly regarding the other prophets, that the *Shechinah* spoke from their throats, that while they were below in this world, they had the revelation of prophecy, which is in Atzilus).

This matter is connected with the study of Torah in the manner of "toiling in Torah," through which "Torah becomes one acquisition," and also "heaven and earth become one acquisition," that physical things become *Elokus*, and consequently, they come without limitations.

**E.** (The Rebbe concluded:)
"And these days are remembered and performed"—as we stand on Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, and especially as we stand already after the *molad* of the moon of the month of Sivan (according to the calculation that we calculate the *molad* according to the mean motion), which pertains to the Jewish people who "count by the moon"—there is certainly already the *hemshech* of Matan Torah, the beginning of which is in the matter of "they came to the wilderness of Sinai."

Therefore, everyone must take upon himself a resolution that he will have a hatred for the matters of this world, and on the other hand, to increase in the study of Torah in the manner of "toiling in Torah," meaning, that even if according to *halacha* one can fulfill his obligation by setting times for Torah (including and especially—a setting in the soul) in the manner of one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening, nevertheless, he should not be satisfied with this, but should increase and toil in Torah.

And since "a person is judged only according to his deeds at that time," the taking of the resolution (to be "toiling in Torah") in itself already activates the *hemshech* of all physical matters, "I will give your rains in their time," with a great increase.
[The Rebbe instructed to play a joyous nigun.]

***

**F.** Our Sages said, "If someone tells you there is wisdom among the nations, believe it; if someone tells you there is Torah among the nations, do not believe it."
This maamar is not speaking about wisdom in general that does not pertain to Torah (other sciences), but about wisdom within the Torah itself, for within the Torah itself there are two matters: the wisdom in Torah, which exists also among the nations, and the Torah in Torah, which is only among the Jewish people.

The explanation of this:
Wisdom—its matter is understanding and comprehension ("farstand"), and this matter exists also in Torah, as it is written, "For it is your wisdom and your understanding in the eyes of the nations." But wisdom (intellect) does not compel that one's conduct in practice be according to the dictates of the intellect. One can understand with his intellect that he must conduct himself in a certain way, and in practice, he conducts himself differently.

Whereas Torah—from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—its matter is a "way-pointer" that instructs a person how to conduct himself in practice, and not only that, but even if the matter is not understood by his intellect, the Torah commands him to do so and so, whether the matter is understood by his intellect or not—not from the side of the wisdom in Torah, but from the side of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) and *bitul* (self-nullification) to the Torah.

This is "If someone tells you there is wisdom among the nations, believe it; if someone tells you there is Torah among the nations, do not believe it"—that among the nations, only the matter of wisdom (in Torah) applies, which they have the ability to understand with their intellect, but the intellectual understanding is not an instruction in life that compels conduct in practice; whereas the matter of Torah (in Torah) exists only among the Jewish people, who possess the *bitul* and dedication to the Torah to fulfill its instructions even when they do not understand the reason.

This matter was innovated at Matan Torah: when "Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai," and said "I am Hashem your G-d," in the singular, that "every single Jew said the utterance is speaking to me"—then there was activated in every Jew a movement of dedication and *bitul* to the Torah.

**G.** And in greater detail:
The movement of dedication and *bitul* to the Torah is expressed in that a Jew fulfills the instructions of the Torah in a way that he does not take anything else into account ("he knows of nothing, and does not calculate with anything"), and not only does he not take physical considerations into account because he has no love for the matters of this world, but furthermore, when he sees that physical matters can be an obstacle to the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, a hatred for physical matters is created in him.

Therefore, also regarding the instruction mentioned about increasing in the study of Torah in the manner of "toiling in Torah" (whereby "I will give your rains in their time" is created with a great increase)—one must conduct oneself according to the instruction of the Torah, Torah from the word *hora'ah*, not (only) from the side of the intellect, but from the side of *kabbalas ol* that is above the intellect, meaning, not to take the conduct of the world according to nature into account, but to fulfill this instruction ("toiling in Torah") even when it appears that this is conduct that is above nature.

**H.** For example:
When a Jew rises from his sleep—he should not immediately think about business matters, for first and foremost he must go to the *beis medrash*, study something before *davening*, *daven*, recite the daily *Tehillim* *shiur*, study a set *shiur* after *davening*, and afterwards return home to eat breakfast—not because he desires to eat, but because this is what Hashem commanded... and he brings a guest with him, and how good if two guests, so that he will have a "quorum" for *Birkas Hamazon*, and only after all this—can he go to his business;
And even when he is in business—he should not invest his entire being into the business and forget everything else, but even in the middle of business he must utilize the opportunity of doing business with a Jew to speak with him in the meantime about *tefillin* or Shabbos, about studying Chassidus, and the like.

**I.** And as is told about the conduct of the great Chassidim in such matters:
The Chassid R' Manish Manesohn was a great merchant in precious stones, and stood in business relations even with the royalty, and nevertheless, his daily schedule was such that he would not manage to begin business matters—after the study of Chassidus, the *avodah* of *davening*, and the study of a set *shiur* after *davening*—until after midday! Once, they came to him with a large order through which he could have earned a large profit, but he could not attend to business matters because he was still in the middle of *davening* or study. After they waited a long time, until the second hour after midday, and someone from his family came to tell him that they were waiting for him with a large order, etc.—he remarked and said: They do not let a Jew have peace ("they don't let a Jew live")... I have not yet put on *Rabbeinu Tam tefillin*, and they are already confusing my mind ("they are already turning my head") about diamonds!... And similarly, there is a story about the Chassid R' Binyamin Kletzker (one of the great Chassidim of the Alter Rebbe), who was a great merchant in timber, and on one of his trips for his timber business, it happened that he became deeply absorbed in his thoughts in matters of Chassidus for several hours... And when they asked him, how is this possible?—he replied: When one thinks in the middle of saying "Echad" about timber-trading—is that not a wonder, and when one thinks in the middle of timber-trading about "Echad"—is that a wonder?!... *On the contrary*: The possibility of thinking in the middle of saying "Echad" about timber-trading—arouses a greater wonder and astonishment! A wonder of wonders!...

**J.** And behold, even though such conduct [to begin business in the middle of the day, or to engage in other matters in the middle of business] is the opposite of the intellect and the opposite of the conduct of the world, for according to the way of nature it is impossible to profit in business in such a way—nevertheless, the conduct of a Jew is according to *Torah*, from the word *hora'ah*, out of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* *that is above the intellect*;
And then, the promise of Hashem is fulfilled, "I will give your rains in their time," in a way that he succeeds in business matters *above nature*, for his wealth is not the wealth of business, but *wealth of Torah* ("he is not a *gvir* from business, but a *gvir* that Torah has made"), and consequently, this is an entirely different matter ("that is something else entirely").

—The Chassid R' Shmuel Gurary once said to one of the merchants who tried to compete with him during a government "tender": "You are competing with me? *The Rebbe* made me a merchant"!... —Of course, in the end, the aforementioned Chassid won that tender.
However, in order for him to have the wealth of Torah, that he should succeed above the way of nature—he must also conduct himself not according to nature, but like a *gvir* of Torah, and in the style of the aforementioned Chassid: a *gvir* of *the Rebbe* ("the Rebbe's *gvir*").

For example:
When a *shaliach* arrives in town—in addition to the fact that he will certainly give him a generous donation, as is fitting *for a gvir of the Rebbe*, furthermore, he will invite the *shaliach* to stay in his home, to eat at his table, "farbrengen with him," and make his stay with him pleasant, and not only that, but he will assist him by taking him in his car to drive him around the city to his destination—for the *shaliach* is a "batlan"... he does not know how to drive a car, and also does not know where one needs to go, and therefore, the *gvir* will take the *shaliach* in his car, and the *shaliach* will be able to fall asleep in the car... knowing that he does not need to worry, since the *gvir* will take him to all the people who can contribute from their money,
And if after all this something is still missing—he will complete all that is lacking from his own...
And after everything is finished, the *gvir* will say to the *shaliach*: Now, I will take you back to your lodging so you can rest, and I will go for some time to attend to business matters...

(The Rebbe concluded:) When the *gvir* conducts himself in such a way (not to take the ways of nature into account, but to conduct himself like a *gvir* of the Rebbe)—then he will truly be a *gvir* of the Rebbe, and will merit to receive the blessing of Hashem in a way that is above nature, "from His full, open, holy—and also *g*dusha (the Rebbe would sometimes pronounce the word *kedusha* in a way that it sounded with a *kuf* and a *gimel*: *k*edusha and *g*dusha)—full and overflowing until it overflows—and expansion."

## Sicha of Erev Shavuos, 5712

- At the conclusion of Maseches Sotah, in his holy room -
(Unedited)

1. At the conclusion of Maseches Sotah, we learned: "Rav Yosef said to the Tanna: Do not teach 'humility' ('When Rabbi died, humility ceased'), for I am here," and Rashi explains: "For I am a humble person."

We must understand:
a) What does Rashi add by explaining Rav Yosef’s words, "Do not teach 'humility' for I am here," as "For I am a humble person"? This is the simple meaning; what is he teaching us?
b) Rav Yosef’s words, "Do not teach [that humility ceased] for I am here," meaning "For I am a humble person"—emphasizing his own virtue of humility—seemingly contradict the very trait of humility itself!

It can be said that these two questions resolve one another. Because of the difficulty that Rav Yosef’s statement "I am here" appears to be the opposite of humility, there is room to interpret his words differently. Therefore, Rashi clarifies that the meaning is "For I am a humble person," as will be explained.

2. Explaining this:
Regarding Rav Yosef’s humility, we find at the end of Maseches Horiyos: "Rav Yosef was a 'Sinai' (possessing vast knowledge of tradition), and Rabbah was an 'uprooter of mountains' (possessing sharp analytical skills). They sent to the scholars there: Which of them should come first? They replied: 'Sinai' is preferable... for everyone needs the master of wheat (meaning Rav Yosef is the master of wheat, for the Mishnah and Braisa are arranged for him by tradition as they were given at Mount Sinai). Even so, Rav Yosef did not accept the position upon himself, and Rabbah reigned... and afterwards Rav Yosef reigned."

Since "Rav Yosef did not accept the position upon himself," believing—due to his great humility—that he was unworthy, it is logical to say that even after he was appointed Nasi ("and afterwards Rav Yosef reigned"), he still believed he was unworthy. His appointment as Nasi was only due to the *humility of the people of his generation*, who appointed him over them.

Based on this, one could interpret Rav Yosef’s words to the Tanna, "Do not teach [that humility ceased] for I am here," as not referring to his own humility (since saying "I am a humble person" is the opposite of humility), but rather that his existence as Nasi ("I am here") serves as proof of the continued existence of the trait of humility *in his generation* (after the death of Rabbi)—the humility of the people of his generation who appointed him over them.

3. In order to negate this interpretation (that the intent is the humility of the people of the generation), Rashi explains: "For I am a humble person."

Rashi’s necessity to interpret Rav Yosef’s words as referring to his own humility ("For I am a humble person") rather than the humility of the people of his generation is derived from the latter part of the statement: "Rav Nachman said to the Tanna: Do not teach [that fear of sin ceased] for I am here." Regarding fear of sin, it is not possible to interpret Rav Nachman’s intent as referring to the people of the generation, but rather *to himself* (that he is a fearer of sin). From this, it is understood that in the first clause as well, regarding humility, the intent is (not the people of the generation, but) *himself* ("For I am a humble person").

Nevertheless, this statement ("I am here," "I am a humble person") does not contradict the concept of humility. Humility does not negate the knowledge of one’s own virtue (including the virtue of humility itself). Rather, even while knowing his own virtue, he does not become arrogant and does not take credit for himself to the point of *yeshus* (self-centeredness), because he calculates that based on the powers granted to him from Above, he should have reached a higher level, and the like.

4. To explain this more deeply, we must first explain the general statement of Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman to the Tanna, "Do not teach... for I am here," which on the face of it is difficult to understand: How can Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman—who are Amoraim—disagree with the words of the Tanna ("When Rabbi died, humility and fear of sin ceased") and say, "Do not teach 'humility' (for I am here)," "Do not teach 'fear of sin' (for I am here)"?!

The point of the explanation is this:
The content of the Tanna’s statement, "When Rabbi died, [humility, etc.] ceased," is that the status and condition of the Tzaddik, and especially "Rabbi," the Nasi and leader of the generation, touches and relates to all the people of the generation. For even though the level of the Tzaddik is incomparably higher than the level of the people of the generation, he influences them, such that the greater the level of the Tzaddik, the greater the level of the people of the generation—according to their own level, at least. Therefore, "When Rabbi died, [humility, etc.] ceased," because since he departed from the world and ascended to a higher world, all the elevations he effected for the people of the generation were hidden.

Regarding this matter—that since the level of the entire generation depends on the Nasi of the generation, then "when Rabbi died," the elevations were hidden—Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman do not disagree.

However, they still say to the Tanna, "Do not teach 'humility' for I am here," "Do not teach 'fear of sin' for I am here," because:
The deficiency caused by the passing of Rabbi is primarily regarding lofty matters connected with the perfection of *avodah* in an internal way. However, regarding lesser matters that are on the level of *makif* (encompassing light), since even after the passing, an impression of the Tzaddik remains in the capacity of *makif* [and it exerts its influence on all who are connected to him, even the lesser among them, and even those who only acknowledge him], these matters remain even after Rabbi died.

Therefore, Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman say to the Tanna, "Do not teach 'humility' for I am here," "Do not teach 'fear of sin' for I am here"—because their level in the matter of humility and fear of sin is (in their opinion) a *lesser* level, and therefore it continues even after Rabbi died, through the influence from the level of *makif*.

This matter is hinted at by Rashi in his explanation of Rav Yosef’s words, "Do not teach 'humility' for I am here," as "For I am a humble person"—that this is a *lesser* level of humility. And as mentioned, Rashi’s necessity is from the latter part of the statement, Rav Nachman’s words, "Do not teach 'fear of sin' for I am here," which is a lesser level of fear, as will be explained.

5. Regarding the words of Rav Nachman—"Do not teach 'fear of sin' for I am here":
In fear, there are many levels, among them: fear of Hashem, as it is written, "Let all the earth fear Hashem," fear of Elokim, etc., up to the lowest level—*fear of sin* alone.

Among the differences between them is that fear of Hashem or fear of Elokim is from an *internal* knowledge and feeling of holiness. Conversely, fear of sin is from the *makif* feeling of holiness alone. That is, even though he does not have internal knowledge and feeling of holiness (which is why he does not relate to fear of Hashem or fear of Elokim), nevertheless, he fears for his soul from something that contradicts and opposes holiness, to the point that he flees from it as one flees from death. For, from the *makif* of holiness (even though it is not in his interiority), he feels at least that the negation and deficiency (sin, *chet*, from the word *chisaron*—deficiency) of holiness is an impossible thing.

This matter is emphasized most strongly in Rav Nachman.
By way of introduction—there are differing opinions as to who "Rav Nachman" refers to, and Rashi follows his own view that the anonymous "Rav Nachman" is Rav Nachman bar Yitzchak. Moreover, in this *sugya*, there are versions in the Gemara where it is explicitly stated as Rav Nachman bar Yitzchak.

We find in the Gemara that "The mother of Rav Nachman bar Yitzchak was told by the astrologers: Your son will be a thief. She did not let him uncover his head. She said to him: Cover your head so that the fear of Heaven will be upon you... One day... his head covering fell off..."

From this, it is understood that by his nature, Rav Nachman was prone to undesirable matters (and who knows what status or situation he could have reached), and his fear of Heaven ("fear of Heaven") was from the influence of *covering the head*—the aspect of *makif*—from the *makif* feeling of holiness alone.

6. From this, it is also understood regarding the words of Rav Yosef, "Do not teach 'humility' for I am here"—"For I am a humble person":
In humility and *bitul*, there are generally two levels: (a) *Bitul b'metzius* (nullification of existence)—like a small scholar standing before a very great scholar, who is nullified from his existence entirely. (b) *Bitul hayesh* (nullification of the *yesh*)—where his existence is felt (and he is not nullified from his existence), but since he does not see in himself any great virtue to be arrogant about (knowing that someone else in his place would have reached a higher level, and the like), he is a "humble person."

More deeply—in the root of these matters Above, in the *Sefirah* of *Keter*:
It is stated in *Tikkunei Zohar* that "the *Keter Elyon*, even though it is a bright light, a polished light, it is 'black' before the Cause of all Causes," because "the *Keter* is above all the ten *Sefiros*, therefore it grasps more the *bitul* of how there is no comparison to the Emanator, the *Ein Sof*, therefore it is 'black'... it is in the state of *bitul* and there is no self-exaltation against... the light of the *Ein Sof* which is above the *Keter*."

Now, in the discourses of Chassidus that bring this statement, we sometimes find the expression "black, black" (twice). It can be said that this hints at two modes of *bitul* ("black, black") corresponding to the two modes in the *Sefirah* of *Keter*: (a) The *Sefirah* of *Keter* as it is in its place—its *bitul* is in the manner of total absence of occupying space, *bitul b'metzius*. (b) And the *Sefirah* of *Keter* as it is after its descent from *Malchus* of *Atzilus* to become *Keter* for *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*—its *bitul* is not in the manner of absence of occupying space [and on the contrary: when *Malchus* of *Atzilus* descends and becomes *Keter* for *BYA*, it is a source for the created beings, and it is certainly not in a *bitul* of absence of occupying space], but rather, since it knows its status and condition that it is in a descent from its root and source, it is not in *yeshus*, only *bitul hayesh*.

Among the differences between them is that the *bitul* of absence of occupying space, *bitul b'metzius*, is achieved through "grasping more the *bitul* of how there is no comparison, etc.," an *internal* grasp and feeling. But when this is not in internal grasp and feeling, but only in the aspect of *makif*—then the *bitul* is not in the manner of absence of occupying space, but rather that he is not in *yeshus*, only *bitul hayesh*.

Regarding our subject—the trait of humility of Rav Yosef:
According to the interpretation that Rav Yosef is speaking about the humility of the people of his generation who appointed him over them even though in his opinion he is unworthy—Rav Yosef’s humility is very great—that he does not feel himself to be an existence at all, absence of occupying space. Therefore, his appointment as Nasi is perceived by him as the humility of the people of his generation. Conversely, according to Rashi’s interpretation, "For I am a humble person"—this is a *lesser* level of humility—where his existence is felt (and not in the manner of absence of occupying space), but he does not take credit for himself, etc.

As mentioned, Rashi’s necessity to interpret that Rav Yosef is speaking about a lesser level of humility ("For I am a humble person") is from the fact that Rav Nachman also speaks about a lesser level of fear of sin. This is the common point in the statements of Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman to the Tanna, "Do not teach... for I am here"—that regarding a lesser level of humility and fear of sin, which is from the aspect of *makif*, one should not teach "When Rabbi died, [humility, etc.] ceased," because the lesser level remains even after the death of Rabbi, since the influence of Rabbi remains from the aspect of *makif* (as mentioned in section 4).

7. One should add and connect the content of the conclusion of the Maseches with the days of *Sefirah* [as per the words of the Rebbe Rayatz, that during the days of *Sefirah*, 49 days, it is customary to study Maseches Sotah, which has 49 pages, one page per day]—the days between Pesach and *Atzeres*—the days of preparation for the Giving of the Torah:

The content of the conclusion of the Maseches in the words of Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman is that there is importance and virtue even in lesser levels of humility and fear of sin that do not penetrate internally but only in a *makif* way.

This matter touches and relates to the preparation for the Giving of the Torah:
It is known that the difference between before the Giving of the Torah and after the Giving of the Torah is completely incomparable. For even though they fulfilled the Torah before the Giving of the Torah, it was in the category of "one who is not commanded and fulfills," and it is not comparable to the fulfillment of *mitzvos* after the Giving of the Torah as "one who is commanded and fulfills."

Similarly, regarding the time of the Giving of the Torah each and every year—a revelation of a new light is created ("a new, higher light that had not yet shone since the days of the world") in the general matter of the Giving of the Torah. Regarding the innovation in the Giving of the Torah of this year, the status and condition of before it is considered like before the Giving of the Torah (similar to "not commanded and fulfills").

Thus, even though before the Giving of the Torah (and similarly before the time of the Giving of the Torah each year) the Jewish people were not vessels for the revelation of the Giving of the Torah in an internal way—to the extent that "at every word their souls departed, etc."—nevertheless, it was sufficient for them to be able to receive the Torah in an internal way, in understanding and grasp within human intellect.

(And the Rebbe concluded:)
And similarly regarding the *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah)—at the time of the Giving of the Torah, the *Pnimiyus HaTorah* was in concealment. Afterwards, it was revealed in the general Torah of Chassidus by the Baal Shem Tov and his students—in a *makif* way, letters only—until the revelation of the Torah of Chassidus Chabad, by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe and his successors, who clothed the *Pnimiyus HaTorah* in understanding and grasp within human intellect. Thus, all the Jewish people, from small to great ("young children and old Jews"), study Chassidus and understand Chassidus, and through this, they draw down and effect the coming of Moshiach ("they pull down Moshiach") below ten *tefachim*.

## With the help of Hashem. The night of the first day of Shavuos - before dawn - 5712

(An unedited transcript)

"Five acquisitions did the Holy One, blessed be He, acquire in His world..." Torah is one acquisition, heaven and earth are one acquisition, Avraham is one acquisition, Yisrael is one acquisition, and the Beis Hamikdash is one acquisition. "Torah, from where do we know? As it is written..." and it brings proofs from verses that all five are called by the name "acquisition." Now, it has been explained previously that when it says "acquire in His world," it specifically means *His* world, excluding (not only the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*, the *alma d’puroda* where there is room for the error that there are two authorities, Heaven forbid, but) even the world of *Atzilus*. For although the world of *Atzilus* is a world of unity—"He and His life are one, He and His causalities are one"—nevertheless, there is within it the differentiation of the aspect of "He," the aspect of "His life," and the aspect of "His causalities," and likewise there is the differentiation of the ten *Sefiros*. Therefore, the true meaning of "His world" refers to the level above *Atzilus*, which is called in the books of Kabbalah by the name *Akkudim*, where all are included in one vessel.

Based on this, we can also understand the matter of "Torah is one acquisition." The act of acquisition is not only regarding the Torah as it descended into *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah* (starting from the descent from *Atzilus* to *Beriah*—of which it is said, "Your Torah which is in *Atzilus* that You taught us in *Beriah*"—down to the descent below to be enclothed in physical things, "to Egypt you descended," etc.) to elevate it to the world of *Atzilus* (which is called an acquisition, similar to an acquisition in the literal sense, which is nothing but a transfer from one domain to another; the object that was initially in the domain of the seller becomes revealed to the buyer, indicating that this is not a new creation *ex nihilo*, but merely the revelation of what was hidden, which is the level of the world of *Atzilus*). Rather, it also applies to the Torah as it is in the world of *Atzilus*, where the act of acquisition is performed to elevate it to the level above *Atzilus*—specifically "His world." For regarding the Torah, it is written, "I was with Him as an *amon* (nurtured child), and I was a delight day by day," which are two levels in the Torah. "I was a delight day by day" refers to the level of Torah of which it is said, "Two thousand years before the world, the Torah preceded" (this is "day by day," the "day" of the Holy One, blessed be He, being a thousand years). "Two thousand" (*alpayim*) is from the root *aalfecha chochmah aalfecha binah* (I will teach you wisdom, I will teach you understanding), the aspect of *Chochmah* and *Binah* of *Atzilus*, which is the level of Torah in the world of *Atzilus*. And what is written, "I was with Him as an *amon*," refers to the level of Torah as it is above *Atzilus*, of which it is said, "And there was a voice from above the firmament." "Voice" refers to the Torah, and "voice from above the firmament" refers to the level of Torah as it is above the firmament of the world of *Atzilus*.

Furthermore, it is explained that the act of acquisition in the Torah is accomplished specifically through the *avodah* of man. For although at the beginning of creation all matters were from the perspective of "for He desires kindness," afterwards, and especially after the giving of the Torah, all matters are accomplished specifically through the *avodah* of Yisrael. And this is the continuation of the matter: "Torah is one acquisition... Yisrael is one acquisition"—that through the *avodah* of Yisrael, who perform the act of acquisition within themselves, they also perform the act of acquisition in the Torah. Likewise, regarding the act of acquisition in the Torah to elevate it to the level above the world of *Atzilus*—this was the *avodah* of Dovid, who would connect the Torah from above with the Holy One, blessed be He. That is, the connection of the Torah from above with the Holy One, blessed be He—to elevate the Torah that is in the world of *Atzilus* to the level above *Atzilus*—was accomplished specifically through the *avodah* of Dovid. For the *avodah* of Dovid was in the manner of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke) specifically, as our Sages said that he established the yoke of *teshuvah*, and he accepted upon himself the yoke of Torah and the yoke of *mitzvos*. Through this, the matter of acquisition was accomplished within himself, and therefore he also accomplished the matter of acquisition in the Torah from above, to elevate it to the level above *Atzilus* and to connect it to the Holy One, blessed be He.

2) Now, the general *avodah* of Yisrael through which the act of acquisition is accomplished is the *avodah* of the souls of Yisrael as they descended below to be enclothed in bodies specifically. The point is that although the descent of the *neshamah* below is a very great descent, nevertheless, this descent is for the sake of an ascent. Through its descent below to be enclothed in a body, it reaches a higher level than it had by itself before its descent below. Therefore, specifically through its *avodah* in its descent below to be enclothed in a body, it accomplishes the matter of acquisition.

We must explain why it is specifically through the *avodah* of the *neshamah* in its descent below to be enclothed in a body that the *neshamah* is elevated to a higher level than it was before its descent. For on the face of it, this is not understood, as it is known that every ascent is by means of "wings," which is the concept of *ahavah* and *yirah* (love and fear) that are called "wings," through which the ascent of the *neshamah* is accomplished. However, regarding the ascent that is accomplished through the *avodah* of the *neshamah* in its descent below to be enclothed in a body, one cannot say that the ascent is through the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* that occurs in the *neshamah* itself while it is enclothed in a body. For the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* while it is below have no value or comparison at all to the level of *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* while it is above, as is explained in *Tanya* that even if a *tzaddik gamur* serves Hashem with *yirah* and great *ahavah* in *taanugim* (delights), he will not reach the level of his *dveikus* in Hashem with *dchilu* and *rechimu* (fear and love) before his descent into this material world—not at all, not even a fraction, and there is no value or comparison between them. This is due to the concealment and hiding of the body, which creates a state of materiality and *yeshus* (selfhood), etc., from which even through much *avodah* one cannot be completely free. To the extent that even a *tzaddik gamur* serving Hashem with *yirah* and *ahavah* in *taanugim* is not completely *batel* in existence, but is a distinct entity who fears Hashem and loves Him; there is a "someone" who loves. If so, how is it possible that through the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* below (which have no value or comparison to the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* above), the *neshamah* is elevated to a level higher than it was before its descent below, when it then stood in an arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* incomparably higher?

3) This will be understood according to what is known, that the descent of the *neshamah* below is in such a way that not the entire *neshamah* is enclothed in the body, but only an illumination and a part of the *neshamah*. However, the essence of the *neshamah* and the *etzem* (core) of the *neshamah* remains as a *makif* (encompassing light) over the body, and is called in the language of our Sages by the name *mazal*, which is the concept of "their *mazal* sees." This matter applies to all levels of the descent of the *neshamah* below. For regarding the souls of Yisrael, it is written, "You are children to Hashem your God," and they cascaded and descended below through the *seder hishtalshelus* of the four worlds: *Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*. From this it is understood that just as in the descent of the *neshamah* below to be enclothed in a body there is the aspect of *mazal*—which is the *makif* that remains above in the ten *Sefiros* of *Malchus* of *Asiyah*—so too in the level of the *neshamah* in the world of *Asiyah* there is the aspect of *mazal* in the ten *Sefiros* of *Malchus* of *Yetzirah*. And likewise in the level of the *neshamah* in the world of *Yetzirah* there is the aspect of *mazal* in the ten *Sefiros* of *Malchus* of *Beriah*, and likewise in the level of the *neshamah* in the world of *Beriah* there is the aspect of *mazal* in the ten *Sefiros* of *Malchus* of *Atzilus*, up to its root in the aspect of *Chochmah* of *Atzilus*, which is the aspect of "it is pure." And since in the *neshamah* enclothed in the body there is the aspect of *mazal* which is the level of the *neshamah* that is in *Asiyah*, whose *mazal* is the level of the *neshamah* that is in *Yetzirah*, etc., up to the aspect of "it is pure" that is in *Atzilus*, it follows that the *neshamah* as it has descended and been enclothed in a body has a connection and bond also with the aspect of "it is pure" that is in *Atzilus*. And of this it is written, "Yaakov is the cord of His inheritance"—like a cord that is held and tied from above to below, such that when one shakes its lower end, at that very moment the whole thing shakes, including its upper end, all at once. And likewise the reverse: when one shakes its upper end, the lower end also shakes automatically. From this it is understood that when the *neshamah* below, which is enclothed in a body, is aroused in *ahavah* and *yirah*, this causes an arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* in all the levels of the *neshamah* above, up to the aspect of "it is pure," in every level according to its nature.

However, since through the *avodah* of the *neshamah* in its enclothement in a body the *neshamah* is elevated to a level higher than it was before its descent, it must be that the superiority of the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* below is not only that through it an arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* is caused in all the levels of the *neshamah* above (for the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* above existed even before its descent below), but rather that there is a superiority in the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* while it is below compared to the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* while it is above.

The point is that the superiority of the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* enclothed in a body is due to the enclothement in the *nefesh habehamis* (animal soul) specifically. For the *nefesh habehamis*, all its matters are not according to *taam vadaas* (intellectual reason), but rather below *taam vadaas*. Therefore, when the *nefesh habehamis* is aroused in *ahavah* and *yirah* for *Elokus* (Divinity) (through the *nefesh elokis* enclothed within it), this is also not according to *taam vadaas*, but below *taam vadaas*. However, this matter is also connected with a level that is above *taam vadaas*, as is known that matters that are below *taam vadaas* have a connection and relevance to what is above *taam vadaas*. And through the descent of the *neshamah* and its enclothement in the *nefesh habehamis*, the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *nefesh elokis* also becomes in a manner that is above *taam vadaas*. This is the superiority of the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* below compared to the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* above: the *ahavah* and *yirah* of the *neshamah* above are according to *taam vadaas*, whereas through its descent below to be enclothed in the *nefesh habehamis*, it attains an *ahavah* and *yirah* that is above *taam vadaas*.

4) The explanation of this matter: It is known that there are two types of *ahavah*: *ahavah zuta* (lesser love) and *ahavah rabbah* (great love). *Ahavah zuta* is love that comes through intellectual contemplation, which is love that is according to *taam vadaas*. *Ahavah rabbah* is a natural and essential love that is above *taam vadaas*. Now, the *avodah* of the *neshamah* by itself (as it is above) is primarily in the matter of *hasagah* (intellectual grasp) specifically. As is known, this is the difference between souls and angels: for angels, their *ahavah* and *yirah* are natural *ahavah* and *yirah*. And even the higher angels in the world of *Beriah*, whose *avodah* is with intellectual *dchilu* and *rechimu* (as it is in *Etz Chaim* and brought in *Tanya*), it is not in such a way that the primary thing is the contemplation and intellectual grasp that becomes the source for the *midos* (emotions). Rather, the intellect is only a cause to arouse and reveal the natural *midos*. The difference between the angels of *Beriah* and the angels of *Yetzirah* is that the *avodah* of the angels of *Yetzirah* is only with natural *dchilu* and *rechimu* alone—that is, they have no intellectual contemplation (not even as a cause) to arouse the *midos*. Whereas the *avodah* of the angels of *Beriah* is with intellectual *dchilu* and *rechimu*, where the intellect is at least a cause to arouse and reveal the *midos*. But even so, the *midos* themselves are not intellectual *midos*, but natural *midos*, because the intellect is only a cause to arouse and reveal the natural *midos*. However, the *avodah* of the souls is primarily in the matter of *hasagah* specifically, and their *midos* are also intellectual *midos*—that is, love that is according to *taam vadaas*. From this comes the difference between angels and souls also in the manner of their *ahavah* and *yirah*: angels always stand in a state of outpouring, yearning, and longing to exit their existence (from their substance). As it is in the *Midrash* that the saying of "Kadosh" three times by the angels is over the course of the twelve hours of the day, because when they say "Kadosh" once, they become *batel* in existence and their soul does not return to them until four hours later, and likewise the second time, etc. Thus, the saying of "Kadosh" three times is over the twelve hours of the day, because each time they say "Kadosh," they stand in longing for four hours. This means their *ahavah* and *yirah* are in a manner of longing and exiting their existence. Not so for souls, whose primary *avodah* is in *hasagah* and *taam vadaas*; their *ahavah* and *yirah* are in measure and limit, and it is impossible for them to be in a state of *klos hanefesh* (soul-expiration), because the source of the *ahavah* and *yirah* is the intellect that gives birth to them. Therefore, the *ahavah* and *yirah* cannot transcend (rise above) their source, which is the intellect.

5) However, through the descent of the *neshamah* below to be enclothed in a body and *nefesh habehamis*, the *neshamah* also attains an *ahavah rabbah* that is above *taam vadaas*. The point is that it is known that the *nefesh elokis* is from the aspect of *tikkun* (rectification), and the *nefesh habehamis* has its root from the world of *tohu* (chaos). And since *tikkun* is primarily *mochin* (intellect) and *tohu* is primarily *midos* which are in the greatest intensity, therefore, the primary *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* by itself is according to *taam vadaas*. Through its descent to be enclothed in the *nefesh habehamis*, which has its root from *tohu*, it also attains an *ahavah rabbah* that is above *taam vadaas*. Furthermore, when the *nefesh elokis* performs its work in refining the *nefesh habehamis*, it then reaches a level that is even above the root of the *nefesh habehamis*, which is in the aspect of *tohu*.

This will be understood by prefacing the explanation of the general matter of the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis* by the *nefesh elokis*. For on the face of it, since in the *seder hishtalshelus* *tohu* precedes *tikkun*, how does the *nefesh elokis*—which is from *tikkun*—have the ability to perform the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis*, whose root is from *tohu* which is above *tikkun*? But the matter is that there is a level that is above *tohu* and *tikkun*, in which *tohu* and *tikkun* are equal. As it is written, "Is not Esav a brother to Yaakov?" And more than that, *tikkun* is above *tohu*, which is why "I loved Yaakov" specifically. From this aspect (in which *tikkun* is above *tohu*), the power is drawn to the *nefesh elokis* to refine the *nefesh habehamis*. It follows that when the *nefesh elokis* performs its work to refine the *nefesh habehamis* from the perspective of its root in the level where *tikkun* is above *tohu*, it reaches (not only the aspect of *tohu* where the root of the *nefesh habehamis* is, but also) the aspect that is above *tohu* and *tikkun* where *tohu* and *tikkun* are equal (similar to the connection of the *nefesh elokis* and *nefesh habehamis*—the *nefesh elokis* which is from the aspect of *tikkun* and the *nefesh habehamis* whose root is from *tohu*—in the work of the *nefesh elokis* in refining the *nefesh habehamis*). And more than that, it reaches its root in the level where *tikkun* is above *tohu* (from which it is drawn the power to refine the *nefesh habehamis*, as mentioned above). This is the matter of the descent of the *neshamah* below, that this descent is for the sake of an ascent—that this ascent is higher than it was above, not only in the world of *Asiyah*, but also in higher levels, and also in the highest level, which is *Chochmah* of *Atzilus*, the aspect of "it is pure" (as mentioned above in section 3). For through its enclothement in the *nefesh habehamis* whose root is from *tohu*, it attains an *ahavah rabbah* that is above *taam vadaas*, and through this, that it performs the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis*, it reaches its root in the aspect that is above *tohu* and *tikkun*, as mentioned above.

6) Now, the ascent of the *neshamah* that is accomplished through its *avodah* below in refining the *nefesh habehamis*, whereby it is elevated from *Atzilus* (where it was before its descent below) to a level above *Atzilus*, is the matter of "Yisrael is one acquisition." Through their *avodah* below in refining the *nefesh habehamis*, the souls of Yisrael are elevated to a level above *Atzilus*—specifically "His world"—and through this they also accomplish the matter of "Torah is one acquisition," to elevate the Torah as it is in the world of *Atzilus* and to connect it to the Holy One, blessed be He, who is above *Atzilus* (as mentioned above in section 1). From this it is understood that the matter of "Torah is one acquisition" is also connected with (and accomplished through) the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis* specifically, just like the matter of "Yisrael is one acquisition."

This will be understood from the general matter of the giving of the Torah, which is accomplished by Yisrael. For since their thought preceded everything—even the Torah, as it is written, "Command the Children of Yisrael, speak to the Children of Yisrael"—they accomplish the matter of "And Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai." The point of this is that the general matter of the giving of the Torah came after and through the fact that "Yisrael encamped there opposite the mountain." "Encamped" (*vayichan*) is in the singular, "as one man with one heart," that the matter of unity was accomplished among them (as is also hinted in the expression "Yisrael is one acquisition"). Through this, the matter of the giving of the Torah was accomplished, which brought about the matter of unity in the world ("heaven and earth are one acquisition"), that the decree was nullified—that the higher realms shall not descend to the lower realms, and the lower realms shall not ascend to the higher realms—and the connection of the higher and lower realms was accomplished, through the fact that the higher realms descended below, "and Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai," and consequently, the lower realms will ascend above. All this came after the preface of the general matter of the exodus from Egypt and the counting of the *Omer*, which includes the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* by itself, and also its *avodah* in refining the *nefesh habehamis*. For regarding the exodus from Egypt, it is written, "Because the people fled," because the evil in the souls of Yisrael was still in its strength; only their goal and desire was for their *nefesh elokis* to exit from the exile of the *Sitra Achra*, which is the impurity of Egypt, and to cleave to Him, blessed be He. This means that first and foremost, there must be the rescue of the *nefesh elokis* that flees from the evil of the *nefesh habehamis*. This matter is accomplished from the perspective of the revelation of light from above, through which the exodus from Egypt occurred, whose effect is only on the *nefesh elokis* alone, for it to have the flight from evil. Afterwards, the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* begins in refining the *nefesh habehamis*, which is the concept of the counting of the *Omer*, as it is written, "And you shall count for yourselves... from the day you bring the *Omer* of the waving, seven complete weeks shall there be." The *Omer* is of barley, the food of an animal, which hints at the *nefesh habehamis*. And of this it is written, "And you shall count," a term of clarity (*behirut*), that one must refine, purify, and illuminate the *nefesh habehamis* so that all its seven *midos* (each of which is included of seven, which is the concept of the seven weeks, which are forty-nine days) will be "complete." That is, not only will they not have a connection to evil, but furthermore, there will not be in them even (a root of) a matter of deficiency. Through this, the matter of "you shall count fifty days" is accomplished, that the fiftieth gate is also drawn from above. It follows that the general matter of the giving of the Torah is accomplished through the *avodah* of Yisrael—both the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* by itself, and the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* in refining the *nefesh habehamis*. This is also the matter of "Torah is one acquisition... Yisrael is one acquisition," that through Yisrael accomplishing the matter of acquisition within themselves, they also accomplish this in the Torah, to elevate it and connect it to the Holy One, blessed be He, who is above *Atzilus*, as mentioned above.

7) This is the content of the entire *maamar* "Five acquisitions did the Holy One, blessed be He, acquire in His world... Torah is one acquisition... Yisrael is one acquisition," that this is not merely a story, but a directive to every single one of Yisrael regarding the general matter of the receiving of the Torah every year. It depends on and is accomplished through the *avodah* of Yisrael, who accomplish the matter of acquisition within themselves (the ascent of the *neshamah* to the level above *Atzilus*) through the *avodah* of refining the *nefesh habehamis*, which is the general matter of the preface of the *avodah* of the exodus from Egypt and the counting of the *Omer* to the receiving of the Torah. One should add that the two crowns that are given at the giving of the Torah also come after the preface of the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* in refining the *nefesh habehamis* specifically. For the *avodah* in refining the *nefesh habehamis* is a matter of *mesiras nefesh* (self-sacrifice) for the *nefesh elokis*, and therefore, through this, they are given the two crowns (a crown that is above *mochin*, which is connected with *mesiras nefesh*). Afterwards, they are also given the Torah, first as a *makif* and then also as a *penimiyus* (internalized), that the receiving of the Torah is accomplished with joy and in an internalized manner.

## B's"d. The Second Day of Shavuos, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

At the time that the Jewish people preceded "we will do" to "we will hear," six hundred thousand ministering angels came to each and every one of the Jewish people and bound two crowns upon him—one corresponding to "we will do" and one corresponding to "we will hear." It is a well-known point of precision in many maamarim, including the maamar of the Rebbe Rayatz of this year, that the conclusion of the Chazal implies that the two crowns are for the matters of "we will do" and "we will hear" themselves, as it says, "one corresponding to 'we will do' and one corresponding to 'we will hear.'" Yet, the beginning of the Chazal implies that the crowns are for the *preceding* of "we will do" to "we will hear." The maamar explains that the preceding of "we will do" to "we will hear" acts upon the matters of "we will do" and "we will hear" themselves so that they are in a more elevated state. From this, it is understood that the bestowing of the crowns for the matters of "we will do" and "we will hear" themselves occurs specifically when they are in the state of having preceded "we will do" to "we will hear."

The concept is as follows: "We will hear" (*nishma*) is similar to *Shema Yisrael*, which is a term for comprehension and understanding. It is the matter of paying attention to each and every mitzvah in its particulars—that is, one sets his heart to hear and listen to how and what the Supreme Will is in the details of the mitzvos. "We will do" (*naaseh*)—which is higher than *nishma*—is the acceptance of the yoke and the *bitul* to the specific desires, to hear every desire and fulfill it. Higher than this is the matter of preceding *naaseh* to *nishma*, which is the acceptance of the yoke and the *bitul* to the *Owner of the Will*, which is a more internal *bitul*.

The difference between them is that in the *avodah* of *nishma*, because it is an *avodah* based on reason and intellect, it is possible for one to say, "This teaching is pleasant, and this teaching is..." and at the very least, even if he does not say "this teaching is not pleasant," in a more subtle sense, it is possible that he will perceive a difference between *mishpatim* (logical laws) and *chukim* (statutes). In *mishpatim*, he will feel more *taanug* than in *chukim*. Likewise, in the *avodah* of *naaseh*, which is *bitul* to the desire alone (and not *bitul* to the Owner of the Will), even though his *bitul* is to fulfill even the mitzvos of *chukim*, nevertheless, it is not comparable to *mishpatim*, where he understands that he must fulfill them because of their own essence. This is unlike *chukim*, where he understands that he must fulfill them because that is the Supreme Will. Since the general *bitul* of *naaseh* is based on reason and intellect, he will have more *taanug* in the fulfillment of *mishpatim*, which are understood by their own nature, than in the fulfillment of *chukim*, which are not understood by their own nature.

However, through the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, which is the matter of *bitul* to the Owner of the Will—meaning that even before the revelation of the desire, he nullifies himself (*leit er zich shoin avek*) to the Owner of the Will—this acts upon the *naaseh* and *nishma* themselves, so that there are no distinctions between one mitzvah and another. Rather, the light and the heavy are equal to him. This is like the servant who is in total *bitul* to the master and has no existence of his own; then, it is considered a privilege for him if the master commands him to do anything at all, without distinction as to what the thing is, through which he can fulfill the master's will. Similarly, in the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, which is the *bitul* to the Owner of the Will in a way that he has no existence of his own at all, there is no difference as to what the desire is.

For in the *avodah* of *naaseh*, which is *bitul* to the desire alone, the *bitul* is in a way where his existence is to fulfill the desire. That is, it is not in a way where he has no existence of his own at all, but rather *his existence* is to fulfill the desire. Since he is an existence, and his existence is to fulfill the desire, there can be a difference for him as to what the desire is (e.g., *mishpatim* or *chukim*). Only when the *avodah* is in the manner of preceding *naaseh* to *nishma*, which is *bitul* to the Owner of the Will—meaning that even before the revelation of the desire, he is in total *bitul* to the Owner of the Will in a way that he has no existence of his own at all—then there will be no differences for him as to what the desire is.

As is known, the power of desire is different from other powers. All powers (such as the power of intellect and the like) come in divisions, and consequently, when one detail is missing, it is only a lack in the perfection of the thing. The desire, however, does not come in divisions, and consequently, when one detail is missing, it is not the desire. Therefore, in the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, which is the *bitul* to the Owner of the Will, the fulfillment of the desire as it is matters, without any difference as to what the desire is. Through this, the *nishma* also becomes more elevated—that is, even when he comes to the understanding and comprehension of the matter, his *taanug* is (not from the understanding and comprehension, but rather) from the fulfillment of the desire of the Owner of the Will. This is why the giving of the crowns corresponding to *naaseh* and *nishma* themselves is specifically through the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, which effects an elevation in the matters of *naaseh* and *nishma* themselves.

b) However, based on this, one must understand: since the virtue of preceding *naaseh* to *nishma* is so great, through which the crowns were given for *naaseh* and *nishma*, there should have been a crown given for the preceding itself. This is a *kal v'chomer*: if for the result of the preceding (the elevation in the matters of *naaseh* and *nishma* through the preceding) there is the matter of the giving of the crowns, then all the more so there should be the giving of a crown for the *avodah* of the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma* itself. If so, there should have been three crowns given: one corresponding to *naaseh*, one corresponding to *nishma*, and one corresponding to the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*. Why were only two crowns given, one for *naaseh* and one for *nishma*, and not for the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*?

The matter is that Chazal said regarding the verse "You shall be holy, for I am holy," that it is a parable of a king for whom the citizens made three crowns. What did the king do? He took one and placed it on his head, and two he placed on the heads of his children. So too, the supernal beings crown three holinesses to the *Ribono shel Olam* every day. What does the *Ribono shel Olam* do? He takes one "Holy" for Himself and gives two to the heads of His children. From this, it is understood also regarding the crowns at the giving of the Torah: the two crowns corresponding to *naaseh* and *nishma* are the crowns that He placed on the heads of His children, and in addition to this, there is also the third crown that is through the *avodah* of the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, but this crown He took for Himself. This is also what is meant by "Go out and see, O daughters of Zion, King Solomon, with the crown with which his mother crowned him on the day of his wedding." Chazal said that "King Solomon" refers to the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is the King to whom peace belongs, and "his mother" refers to the congregation of Israel, and "the day of his wedding" is the giving of the Torah. If so, the meaning of "with the crown with which his mother crowned him" is that at the giving of the Torah, the souls of Israel crowned and adorned the *Ribono shel Olam* with a crown, which is the third crown that is through the *avodah* of the preceding of *naaseh* to *nishma*, which He took for Himself.

The explanation of the matter of the three crowns and their connection to the giving of the Torah will be understood by prefacing what Chazal said regarding what is written, "And there was evening and there was morning, the sixth day." Why the extra letter *hei*? It teaches that the *Ribono shel Olam* made a condition with the works of creation and said to them: "If the Jewish people accept the Torah, you will endure, etc." This is "And there was evening and there was morning, the sixth day"—that the "evening and morning" of the completion of creation depends on the sixth day, which is the sixth of Sivan, on which the Torah was given. That is, until the giving of the Torah, the world did not have true existence, as it was dependent on a condition, and only at the giving of the Torah did the existence of the world come about.

More specifically, Chazal said that the world stands on three things: on Torah, on *avodah*, and on acts of kindness (*gemilus chasadim*). The matter is that the essence of the world's existence is specifically through the *makifim* (encompassing lights). Just as it is in a person, whose essence of existence is from the level of the *makif* of the *neshamah*—which is what we say: "The *neshamah*... is pure; You created it, You fashioned it, and You breathed it into me," which are the details of the levels of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, all of which are in the category of *pnimiyus* (internal)—and afterwards we say, "And You guard it within me," which is the level of the *makif*, through which is the essence of existence. Likewise, in the world, which is called a "great body," its essence of existence is specifically from the level of the *makif*. More specifically, the existence of the world is through the three *makifim* of Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*. This is also the content of the matter of the three crowns and their connection to the giving of the Torah: they are the three *makifim* (for a crown and diadem are *makif*) through which the existence of the world was effected at the giving of the Torah.

c) To understand this, one must first preface the known fact that the general matter of the creation of the worlds is called *Hishtalshelus*, which is from the word *shaloshet* (chain), like a chain made of many links that are attached to one another and descend and extend from above to below. The end of the upper link enters into the beginning of the lower link, and so too the lower one into the one below it, and so it descends and extends from link to link. However, likewise, the lower link is attached and connected to the upper one, and the upper one to the one above it. From this, it is understood that all the links in the chain are connected and belong to one another, until the lowest link is connected and belongs also to the highest link. For even though the end of the lower link is not attached and connected to the link above it, only its beginning is, this is the beginning and end of one link, and consequently, the end of the lower link also belongs to the link above it, and so on up to the highest link. Likewise, the highest link belongs to the link below it, down to the lowest link. Even though the beginning of the upper link is not attached and connected to the link below it, only its end is, this is the beginning and end of one link, and consequently, the beginning of the upper link also belongs to the link below it, down to the lowest link. Its parallel in the creation of the worlds, which is called *Hishtalshelus*, is that all the worlds in the *Seder Hishtalshelus* have a connection to one another.

However, regarding the level above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, there is no value or connection to the created and emanated beings at all. It is known that there is no comparison at all between the emanated beings and the *Atzmus* of *Ohr Ein Sof*. Just as there is no comparison of *Asiyah* to *Atzilus*, there is no comparison of *Atzilus* to *Ohr Ein Sof*. That is, even though within the *Seder Hishtalshelus* itself there is no comparison of *Asiyah* to *Atzilus*, nevertheless, because they are in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, they are connected to one another—that is, they are equal in that they are all created or emanated beings. But regarding the *Ohr Ein Sof* the Emanator, even the world of *Atzilus* has no value at all, to the point that *Atzilus* and *Asiyah* are truly equal.

d) This will be understood through a parable from the *Seder Hishtalshelus* in the human soul: the garments of the soul—thought, speech, and action—whose root is from the *midos*, and the *midos* whose root is from the intellect, and the intellect whose root is from the power of the *maskil* (the intellect-possessor). All these levels belong to one another. The matter is that thought, speech, and action, whose root is in the *midos*, are in a way that there is an inclusion of the thought, speech, and action in the *midos*. For thought, speech, and action are the garments of the soul, like a garment through which the one clothed in it is revealed—that is, the thought, speech, and action reveal the *midos*. Thus, the power of revelation in the *midos* is the matter of the inclusion of thought, speech, and action in the *midos*. Likewise, there is the matter of the *midos* in thought, speech, and action, as the *midos* give vitality to the thought, speech, and action. Similarly, in the *midos* whose root is from the intellect, there is an inclusion of the *midos* in the intellect, which is the matter of the *hispaalus* of the intellect (for *hispaalus* is a different essence than intellect, and it is the matter of the inclusion of the *midos* in the intellect). Likewise, there is the matter of the intellect in the *midos*, as the intellect effects vitality and growth in the *midos*. Similarly, in the intellect whose root is from the power of the *maskil*, even though the revelation of the intellect comes specifically through exertion—which indicates that the power of the *maskil* is not an intellect-existence, and the invention of the intellect from it is like *yesh me'ayin*—nevertheless, since through exertion an intellect is found from it, and nothing but intellect is found from it, it is a source for the intellect. This is the matter of the inclusion of the intellect in the power of the *maskil*. Likewise, there is the matter of the power of the *maskil* in the intellect, as there are matters of the intellect that do not come into understanding and explanation, as in "a great scholar... but he does not return to it," which is from the side of the revelation of the power of the *maskil*. That is, it is not as it remains in concealment in the power of the *maskil*, but as it comes into revelation, only that it is not the revelation of the intellect, but the revelation of the power of the *maskil*. From this, it is understood that there is a connection and belonging between all the details of the levels in the aforementioned *Seder Hishtalshelus*, from the power of the *maskil* to thought, speech, and action.

However, in order for there to be an extension of the powers from the essence of the soul, which is simple in the ultimate sense, this is not by way of *Hishtalshelus*, but by way of *yesh me'ayin*. Its parallel above is that all the details of the levels in the *Seder Hishtalshelus* have value and connection to one another, but they have no value at all regarding the *Ohr Ein Sof* the Emanator, because it is *Ohr Ein Sof* that does not give place for the standing of the worlds, as it is in *Etz Chaim* that at first the *Ohr Ein Sof* filled the void and there was no place for the standing of the worlds, and afterwards He removed His great light to the side and extended a short and thin *Kav*. From this, it is understood that there is no value or connection for the worlds with the *Ohr Ein Sof* the Emanator, for for the coming-into-being of the worlds, there had to be a *Tzimtzum* in the manner of the removal of the light, etc., because it is *Ohr Ein Sof* that is completely above the worlds. That is, the coming-into-being of the worlds from the *Ohr Ein Sof* the Emanator is not by way of *Hishtalshelus*, but by way of *yesh me'ayin*.

e) Now, even though the level of *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum* is above connection to the worlds, as it does not give place for the worlds, nevertheless, there is extended from it into the worlds as they are after the *Tzimtzum* (not only the light of the *Kav* that was clothed in the *Tzimtzum*, but) also from the level of the great circle over which the *Tzimtzum* has no control (even though the *Tzimtzum* touched it). However, in order for its extension to be in the world, it comes through the passage of the *Tzimtzum*, but only by way of a conduit, so it does not change from its essence, and therefore it is in the category of *Ein Sof* like the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum*. As is known, this is one of the explanations regarding the *Hishtalshelus* of the crowns from one another, that even the circles after the *Tzimtzum*, even though they are extended from the *Kav* (as it is in *Etz Chaim* that the *Kav* extends and circles, etc.), nevertheless, they are connected with the level of the great circle before the *Tzimtzum*, which is what is extended only through the conduit of the *Tzimtzum*. This is also the general difference between circles and *yosher* (straight): *yosher* is the light that was clothed in the *Tzimtzum* and its essence changed and it came into division, etc., and circles is the light that came through the conduit of the *Tzimtzum* and its essence did not change, which is why even below it is in the category of *Ein Sof* that is above division.

The parable for this in created beings below is the difference between earth and water. Earth has division, as it is in *Avos D'Rabbi Nosson* that the earth has a head, body, and feet, like the division in a person, where the general vitality in the head is divided into three parts, which are the three *mochin* *Chabad* that are clothed in the three cavities of the brain that are divided from one another. From these three *mochin* branch out the three senses of sight, hearing, and speech (the sense of sight from *Chochma*, the sense of hearing from *Binah*, and the sense of speech from *Daas*, as it is written, "From His mouth is *Daas*." Therefore, the angels are called by the names of beast, lion, and ox, etc., for they do not have *Daas* (that is, *Daas* of the Above, but only *Daas* of the below) and they do not have speech.
